Volere

Requirements Specification Template

\textbf{Edition 16---2012}

by James Robertson \& Suzanne Robertson

principals of the Atlantic Systems Guild

The Volere Requirements Specification Template is intended for use as a
basis for your requirements specifications. The template provides
sections for each of the requirements types appropriate to
today\textquotesingle s software systems. You may download the template
from the Volere site and adapt it to your requirements gathering process
and requirements tool. The template can be used with Requisite, DOORS,
Caliber RM, IRqA and other popular tools see
\url{http://www.volere.co.uk/tools.htm}

The template may not be sold, or used for commercial gain or purposes
other than as a basis for a requirements specification without prior
written permission. The Template may be modified or copied and used for
your requirements work, provided you include the following copyright
notice in any document that uses any part of this template:

\emph{We acknowledge that this document uses material from the Volere
Requirements Specification Template, copyright © 1995 -- 2012 the
Atlantic Systems Guild Limited}.

\hypertarget{volere-1}{%
\section{Volere}\label{volere-1}}

Volere is the result of many years of practice, consulting, and research
in requirements engineering and business analysis. We have packaged our
experience in the form of a generic requirements process, requirements
training, requirements consultancy, requirements audits, a variety of
downloadable guides and articles, a requirements knowledge model and
this requirements template. We also provide requirements
specification-writing services.

The first edition of the Volere Requirements Specification Template was
released in 1995. Since then, organizations from all over the world have
saved time and money by using the template as the basis for discovering,
organizing, and communicating their requirements.

The Volere web site www.volere.co.uk contains articles about the Volere
techniques, experiences of Volere users and case studies, requirements
tools, and other information useful to requirements practitioners.

The Volere requirements process is described in the book \emph{Mastering
the Requirements Process---Second Edition} by Suzanne Robertson and
James Robertson, Addison-Wesley, 2006. ISBN 0-321-41949-9

For more about managing requirements see \emph{Requirements Led Project
Management} by Suzanne Robertson and James Robertson, Addison-Wesley,
2005. ISBN 0-321-65904-X

Updates to this template and instructions for downloading are available
at \href{http://www.volere.co.uk/}{http://www.volere.co.uk}

\textbf{Public seminars} on Volere are run on a regular basis in Europe,
the United States, Australia, and New Zealand. For a schedule of
courses, refer to \href{http://www.volere.co.uk/}{www.volere.co.uk}.

\hypertarget{requirements-types}{%
\section{Requirements Types}\label{requirements-types}}

For ease of use, we have found it convenient to think of requirements as
belonging to a type. There are two reasons for the type: as an aid to
finding the requirements, to be able to group the requirements that are
relevant to a specific expert specialty.

\emph{Functional requirements} are the fundamental or essential subject
matter of the product. They describe what the product has to do or what
processing actions it must take.

\emph{Non-functional requirements} are the properties that the functions
must have, such as performance and usability. Do not be deterred by the
unfortunate name for this kind of requirements, they are as important as
the functional requirements for the product's success.

\emph{Project constraints} are restrictions on the product due to the
budget or the time available to build the product.

\emph{Design constraints} impose restrictions on how the product must be
designed. For example, it might have to be implemented in the hand-held
device being given to major customers, or it might have to use the
existing servers and desktop computers, or any other hardware, software,
or business practice.

\emph{Project drivers} are the business-related forces. For example, the
purpose of the project is a project driver, as are all of the
stakeholders---each for different reasons.

\emph{Project issues} define the conditions under which the project will
be done. Our reason for including them as part of the requirements is to
present a coherent picture of all factors that contribute to the success
or failure of the project and to illustrate how managers can use
requirements as input when managing a project.

\hypertarget{testing-requirements}{%
\section{Testing Requirements}\label{testing-requirements}}

The Volere philosophy is to start testing requirements as soon as you
start writing them. You make a requirement testable by adding its
\emph{fit criterion}. This fit criterion measures the requirement,
making it possible to determine whether a given solution fits the
requirement. If a fit criterion cannot be found for a requirement, then
the requirement is either ambiguous or poorly understood. All
requirements can be measured, and all should carry a fit criterion.

\hypertarget{atomic-requirements-shell}{%
\section{Atomic Requirements Shell}\label{atomic-requirements-shell}}

The requirements shell is a guide to writing each atomic requirement.
The components of the shell (also called a ``snow card'') are identified
below. You might decide to add some additional attributes to provide
traceability necessary for your environment. For example: products that
implement this requirement, version of the software that implements this
requirement, departments who are interested in this requirement, etc.
There are others but do not capriciously add attributes unless they
really help you: every attribute you add needs to be maintained.

This requirements shell can, and should, be automated. When you download
the template you will also find an Excel spreadsheet implementation of
the snow card.

\includegraphics[width=5.8in,height=5.18542in]{vertopal_7b3017d28f8c463495d83dbfa1d97e53/media/image1.jpeg}

\emph{The following discusses and provides examples for each of the
sections of the Volere Requirements Specification Template. For each
section, the Content, Motivation, Considerations, Examples and Form
provide the template user with some guidance for writing each type of
requirement. When you download the template you will also find a
Template Skeleton that you might find convenient to use as the basis for
producing a document.}

\hypertarget{the-purpose-of-the-project}{%
\section{1. The Purpose of the
Project}\label{the-purpose-of-the-project}}

The first section of the template deals with the fundamental reason your
client asked you to build a new product. That is, it describes the
business problem the client faces and explains how the product is
intended to solve the problem.

\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{This part of the specification describes
what we want the product to do and what advantage it will bring to the
overall goals of the work. Do not be too wordy in this section---a brief
explanation of the project's goals is usually more valuable than a long,
rambling treatise. A short, sharp goal will be clearer to the
stakeholders and improve the chances of reaching a consensus for the
goal.

\hypertarget{you-can-use-purpose-advantage-measurement-pam-to-structure-your-goal.}{%
\subsubsection{You can use Purpose, Advantage, Measurement (PAM) to
structure your
goal.}\label{you-can-use-purpose-advantage-measurement-pam-to-structure-your-goal.}}

\hypertarget{purpose-one-sentence-to-explain-the-organisations-reason-for-investing-in-the-project.}{%
\subsubsection{Purpose: one sentence to explain the organisation's
reason for investing in the
project.}\label{purpose-one-sentence-to-explain-the-organisations-reason-for-investing-in-the-project.}}

\hypertarget{advantage-one-sentence-describing-the-benefit-that-the-organization-will-realize-if-the-project-is-successful.}{%
\subsubsection{Advantage: One sentence describing the benefit that the
organization will realize if the project is
successful.}\label{advantage-one-sentence-describing-the-benefit-that-the-organization-will-realize-if-the-project-is-successful.}}

\hypertarget{measurement-one-sentence-or-a-graph-or-diagram-that-quantifies-how-you-will-measure-whether-or-not-the-benefit-has-been-achieved.}{%
\subsubsection{Measurement: One sentence or a graph or diagram that
quantifies how you will measure whether or not the benefit has been
achieved.}\label{measurement-one-sentence-or-a-graph-or-diagram-that-quantifies-how-you-will-measure-whether-or-not-the-benefit-has-been-achieved.}}

\hypertarget{another-form-for-your-goals-might-be-to-use-some-kind-of-goal-model.-for-example-the-extended-enterprise-modelling-language-eeml-includes-a-goal-modelling-technique.-if-your-organization-is-using-enterprise-modelling-then-this-provides-a-connection-between-the-enterprises-strategic-goals-and-the-goal-of-an-individual-project.}{%
\subsubsection{Another form for your goals might be to use some kind of
goal model. For example, the Extended Enterprise Modelling Language
EEML, includes a goal modelling technique. If your organization is using
enterprise modelling then this provides a connection between the
enterprise's strategic goals and the goal of an individual
project.}\label{another-form-for-your-goals-might-be-to-use-some-kind-of-goal-model.-for-example-the-extended-enterprise-modelling-language-eeml-includes-a-goal-modelling-technique.-if-your-organization-is-using-enterprise-modelling-then-this-provides-a-connection-between-the-enterprises-strategic-goals-and-the-goal-of-an-individual-project.}}

\hypertarget{the-stakeholders}{%
\section{2. The Stakeholders}\label{the-stakeholders}}

This section describes the stakeholders---the people who have an
interest in the product. It is worth your while to spend enough time to
accurately determine and describe these people, as the penalty for not
knowing who they are can be very high.

\hypertarget{a.-the-client}{%
\subsection{\texorpdfstring{2a. The Client
}{2a. The Client }}\label{a.-the-client}}

\hypertarget{content-2}{%
\subsubsection{Content}\label{content-2}}

\hypertarget{this-item-gives-the-name-of-the-client-sometimes-referred-to-as-the-sponsor-it-is-permissible-to-have-several-names-but-having-more-than-three-negates-the-point.}{%
\subsubsection{This item gives the name of the client (sometimes
referred to as the sponsor) It is permissible to have several names, but
having more than three negates the
point.}\label{this-item-gives-the-name-of-the-client-sometimes-referred-to-as-the-sponsor-it-is-permissible-to-have-several-names-but-having-more-than-three-negates-the-point.}}

\hypertarget{motivation-2}{%
\subsubsection{Motivation}\label{motivation-2}}

\hypertarget{the-client-has-the-final-say-on-acceptance-of-the-product-and-thus-must-be-satisfied-with-the-product-as-delivered.-you-can-think-of-the-client-as-the-person-who-makes-the-investment-in-the-product.-where-the-product-is-being-developed-for-in-house-consumption-the-same-person-often-fills-the-roles-of-the-client-and-the-customer.-if-you-cannot-find-a-name-for-your-client-then-perhaps-you-should-not-be-building-the-product.}{%
\subsubsection{The client has the final say on acceptance of the
product, and thus must be satisfied with the product as delivered. You
can think of the client as the person who makes the investment in the
product. Where the product is being developed for in-house consumption,
the same person often fills the roles of the client and the customer. If
you cannot find a name for your client, then perhaps you should not be
building the
product.}\label{the-client-has-the-final-say-on-acceptance-of-the-product-and-thus-must-be-satisfied-with-the-product-as-delivered.-you-can-think-of-the-client-as-the-person-who-makes-the-investment-in-the-product.-where-the-product-is-being-developed-for-in-house-consumption-the-same-person-often-fills-the-roles-of-the-client-and-the-customer.-if-you-cannot-find-a-name-for-your-client-then-perhaps-you-should-not-be-building-the-product.}}

\hypertarget{considerations-1}{%
\subsubsection{Considerations}\label{considerations-1}}

\hypertarget{sometimes-when-building-a-package-or-a-product-for-external-users-the-client-is-the-marketing-department.-in-this-case-a-person-from-the-marketing-department-must-be-named-as-the-client.}{%
\subsubsection{Sometimes, when building a package or a product for
external users, the client is the marketing department. In this case, a
person from the marketing department must be named as the
client.}\label{sometimes-when-building-a-package-or-a-product-for-external-users-the-client-is-the-marketing-department.-in-this-case-a-person-from-the-marketing-department-must-be-named-as-the-client.}}

\subsubsection{Motivation}\label{motivation-3}}

\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{The customer is ultimately responsible

\hypertarget{examples-1}{%
\subsubsection{Examples}\label{examples-1}}

\hypertarget{users-can-come-from-wide-variety-of-sometimes-unexpected-sources.-consider-the-possibility-of-your-users-being-clerical-staff-shop-workers-managers-highly-trained-operators-the-general-public-casual-users-passers-by-illiterate-people-tradesmen-students-test-engineers-foreigners-children-lawyers-remote-users-people-using-the-system-over-the-telephone-or-an-internet-connection-emergency-workers-and-so-on.}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Users can come from wide variety of
(sometimes unexpected) sources. Consider the possibility of your users
being clerical staff, shop workers, managers, highly trained operators,
the general public, casual users, passers-by, illiterate people,
tradesmen, students, test engineers, foreigners, children, lawyers,
remote users, people using the system over the telephone or an Internet
connection, emergency workers, and so on.
}{Users can come from wide variety of (sometimes unexpected) sources. Consider the possibility of your users being clerical staff, shop workers, managers, highly trained operators, the general public, casual users, passers-by, illiterate people, tradesmen, students, test engineers, foreigners, children, lawyers, remote users, people using the system over the telephone or an Internet connection, emergency workers, and so on. }}\label{users-can-come-from-wide-variety-of-sometimes-unexpected-sources.-consider-the-possibility-of-your-users-being-clerical-staff-shop-workers-managers-highly-trained-operators-the-general-public-casual-users-passers-by-illiterate-people-tradesmen-students-test-engineers-foreigners-children-lawyers-remote-users-people-using-the-system-over-the-telephone-or-an-internet-connection-emergency-workers-and-so-on.}}

\hypertarget{content-6}{%

\hypertarget{personas-name-age-job-family-hobbies-where-they-live-favourite-food-favourite-music-likes-dislikes-where-they-go-on-holiday-attitude-to-technology-attitude-to-money-or-any-other-characteristic-that-could-influence-the-way-that-the-persona-thinks-of-the-product.-it-helps-if-you-include-a-photograph-or-drawing-of-the-imagined-person.}{%

imagined
person.}\label{personas-name-age-job-family-hobbies-where-they-live-favourite-food-favourite-music-likes-dislikes-where-they-go-on-holiday-attitude-to-technology-attitude-to-money-or-any-other-characteristic-that-could-influence-the-way-that-the-persona-thinks-of-the-product.-it-helps-if-you-include-a-photograph-or-drawing-of-the-imagined-person.}}

\hypertarget{motivation-6}{%
\subsubsection{Motivation}\label{motivation-6}}

\hypertarget{by-having-one-or-more-limit-it-to-3-personas-you-can-make-the-requirements-specific-to-the-people-you-are-trying-to-satisfy.-this-is-a-particularly-effective-technique-if-you-are-specifying-the-requirements-for-a-consumer-product-or-a-product-that-will-be-used-by-members-of-the-public.}{%
\subsubsection{By having one or more (limit it to 3) personas you can
make the requirements specific to the people you are trying to satisfy.
This is a particularly effective technique if you are specifying the
requirements for a consumer product or a product that will be used by
members of the
public.}\label{by-having-one-or-more-limit-it-to-3-personas-you-can-make-the-requirements-specific-to-the-people-you-are-trying-to-satisfy.-this-is-a-particularly-effective-technique-if-you-are-specifying-the-requirements-for-a-consumer-product-or-a-product-that-will-be-used-by-members-of-the-public.}}

\hypertarget{form-6}{%
\subsubsection{Form}\label{form-6}}

\hypertarget{a-profile-containing-the-life-story-of-the-persona.-include-a-photograph-or-drawing-of-the-person.-the-profile-can-be-in-the-form-of-a-document-that-you-use-to-introduce-project-participants-to-the-persona.-you-can-also-put-the-profile-onto-a-large-format-a3-card-that-you-display-at-meetings-to-remind-participants-about-whose-requirements-you-are-trying-to-discover.-another-idea-is-to-build-a-storyboard-of-the-personas-life.-also-you-can-make-a-website-for-the-persona-and-keep-himher-alive-by-adding-more-about-the-personas-everyday-life.-all-of-these-forms-of-capturing-and-communicating-the-persona-are-intended-to-help-people-think-of-the-persona-as-a-real-user-with-specific-rather-than-general-real-requirements.}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{A profile containing the life story of
the persona. Include a photograph or drawing of the person. The profile
can be in the form of a document that you use to introduce project
participants to the persona. You can also put the profile onto a large
format, A3, card that you display at meetings to remind participants
about whose requirements you are trying to discover. Another idea is to
build a storyboard of the persona's life. Also you can make a website
for the persona and keep him/her alive by adding more about the
persona's everyday life. All of these forms of capturing and
communicating the persona are intended to help people think of the
persona as a real user with specific, rather than general, real
requirements.
}{A profile containing the life story of the persona. Include a photograph or drawing of the person. The profile can be in the form of a document that you use to introduce project participants to the persona. You can also put the profile onto a large format, A3, card that you display at meetings to remind participants about whose requirements you are trying to discover. Another idea is to build a storyboard of the persona's life. Also you can make a website for the persona and keep him/her alive by adding more about the persona's everyday life. All of these forms of capturing and communicating the persona are intended to help people think of the persona as a real user with specific, rather than general, real requirements. }}\label{a-profile-containing-the-life-story-of-the-persona.-include-a-photograph-or-drawing-of-the-person.-the-profile-can-be-in-the-form-of-a-document-that-you-use-to-introduce-project-participants-to-the-persona.-you-can-also-put-the-profile-onto-a-large-format-a3-card-that-you-display-at-meetings-to-remind-participants-about-whose-requirements-you-are-trying-to-discover.-another-idea-is-to-build-a-storyboard-of-the-personas-life.-also-you-can-make-a-website-for-the-persona-and-keep-himher-alive-by-adding-more-about-the-personas-everyday-life.-all-of-these-forms-of-capturing-and-communicating-the-persona-are-intended-to-help-people-think-of-the-persona-as-a-real-user-with-specific-rather-than-general-real-requirements.}}

\hypertarget{key-users-they-are-critical-to-the-continued-success-of-the-product.-give-greater-importance-to-requirements-generated-by-this-category-of-user.}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{● Key users: They are critical to the
continued success of the product. Give greater importance to
requirements generated by this category of user.
}{● Key users: They are critical to the continued success of the product. Give greater importance to requirements generated by this category of user. }}\label{key-users-they-are-critical-to-the-continued-success-of-the-product.-give-greater-importance-to-requirements-generated-by-this-category-of-user.}}

\hypertarget{secondary-users-they-will-use-the-product-but-their-opinion-of-it-has-no-effect-on-its-long-term-success.-where-there-is-a-conflict-between-secondary-users-requirements-and-those-of-key-users-the-key-users-take-precedence.}{%
\subsubsection{● Secondary users: They will use the product, but their
opinion of it has no effect on its long-term success. Where there is a
conflict between secondary users' requirements and those of key users,
the key users take
precedence.}\label{secondary-users-they-will-use-the-product-but-their-opinion-of-it-has-no-effect-on-its-long-term-success.-where-there-is-a-conflict-between-secondary-users-requirements-and-those-of-key-users-the-key-users-take-precedence.}}

\hypertarget{unimportant-users-this-category-of-user-is-given-the-lowest-priority.-it-includes-infrequent-unauthorized-and-unskilled-users-as-well-as-people-who-misuse-the-product.}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{● Unimportant users: This category of
user is given the lowest priority. It includes infrequent, unauthorized,
and unskilled users, as well as people who misuse the product.
}{● Unimportant users: This category of user is given the lowest priority. It includes infrequent, unauthorized, and unskilled users, as well as people who misuse the product. }}\label{unimportant-users-this-category-of-user-is-given-the-lowest-priority.-it-includes-infrequent-unauthorized-and-unskilled-users-as-well-as-people-who-misuse-the-product.}}

\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{The percentage of the type of user is
intended to assess the amount of consideration given to each category of
user.
}{The percentage of the type of user is intended to assess the amount of consideration given to each category of user. }}\label{the-percentage-of-the-type-of-user-is-intended-to-assess-the-amount-of-consideration-given-to-each-category-of-user.}}

\hypertarget{motivation-7}{%
\subsubsection{Motivation}\label{motivation-7}}

\hypertarget{if-some-users-are-considered-to-be-more-important-to-the-product-or-to-the-organization-then-this-preference-should-be-stated-because-it-should-affect-the-way-that-you-design-the-product.-for-instance-you-need-to-know-if-there-is-a-large-customer-group-who-has-specifically-asked-for-the-product-and-for-which-if-they-do-not-get-what-they-want-the-results-could-be-a-significant-loss-of-business.}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{If some users are considered to be more
important to the product or to the organization, then this preference
should be stated because it should affect the way that you design the
product. For instance, you need to know if there is a large customer
group who has specifically asked for the product, and for which, if they
do not get what they want, the results could be a significant loss of
business.
}{If some users are considered to be more important to the product or to the organization, then this preference should be stated because it should affect the way that you design the product. For instance, you need to know if there is a large customer group who has specifically asked for the product, and for which, if they do not get what they want, the results could be a significant loss of business. }}\label{if-some-users-are-considered-to-be-more-important-to-the-product-or-to-the-organization-then-this-preference-should-be-stated-because-it-should-affect-the-way-that-you-design-the-product.-for-instance-you-need-to-know-if-there-is-a-large-customer-group-who-has-specifically-asked-for-the-product-and-for-which-if-they-do-not-get-what-they-want-the-results-could-be-a-significant-loss-of-business.}}

\hypertarget{some-users-may-be-listed-as-having-no-impact-on-the-product.-these-users-will-make-use-of-the-product-but-have-no-vested-interest-in-it.-in-other-words-these-users-will-not-complain-nor-will-they-contribute.-any-special-requirements-from-these-users-will-have-a-lower-design-priority.}{%
\subsubsection{Some users may be listed as having no impact on the
product. These users will make use of the product, but have no vested
interest in it. In other words, these users will not complain, nor will
they contribute. Any special requirements from these users will have a
lower design
priority.}\label{some-users-may-be-listed-as-having-no-impact-on-the-product.-these-users-will-make-use-of-the-product-but-have-no-vested-interest-in-it.-in-other-words-these-users-will-not-complain-nor-will-they-contribute.-any-special-requirements-from-these-users-will-have-a-lower-design-priority.}}

\hypertarget{form-7}{%
\subsubsection{Form}\label{form-7}}

\hypertarget{include-the-user-importance-rating-on-your-user-characteristics-spreadsheet-see-2d-for-the-information-of-the-core-project-team.-depending-on-the-culture-of-your-organization-you-might-need-to-treat-this-as-sensitive-information.}{%
\subsubsection{Include the user importance rating on your user
characteristics spreadsheet, see 2d, for the information of the core
project team. Depending on the culture of your organization, you might
need to treat this as sensitive
information.}\label{include-the-user-importance-rating-on-your-user-characteristics-spreadsheet-see-2d-for-the-information-of-the-core-project-team.-depending-on-the-culture-of-your-organization-you-might-need-to-treat-this-as-sensitive-information.}}

\hypertarget{where-appropriate-attach-to-the-category-of-user-a-statement-of-the-participation-that-you-think-will-be-necessary-for-those-users-to-provide-the-requirements.-describe-the-contribution-that-you-expect-these-users-to-providefor-example-business-knowledge-interface-prototyping-or-usability-requirements.-if-possible-assess-the-minimum-amount-of-time-that-these-users-must-spend-for-you-to-be-able-to-determine-the-complete-requirements.}{%

\hypertarget{motivation-8}{%
\subsubsection{Motivation}\label{motivation-8}}

\hypertarget{many-projects-fail-through-lack-of-user-participation-sometimes-because-the-required-degree-of-participation-was-not-made-clear.-when-people-have-to-make-a-choice-between-getting-their-everyday-work-done-and-working-on-a-new-project-the-everyday-work-usually-takes-priority.-this-requirement-makes-it-clear-from-the-outset-that-specified-user-resources-must-be-allocated-to-the-project.}{%
\subsubsection{Many projects fail through lack of user participation,
sometimes because the required degree of participation was not made
clear. When people have to make a choice between getting their everyday
work done and working on a new project, the everyday work usually takes
priority. This requirement makes it clear, from the outset, that
specified user resources must be allocated to the
project.}\label{many-projects-fail-through-lack-of-user-participation-sometimes-because-the-required-degree-of-participation-was-not-made-clear.-when-people-have-to-make-a-choice-between-getting-their-everyday-work-done-and-working-on-a-new-project-the-everyday-work-usually-takes-priority.-this-requirement-makes-it-clear-from-the-outset-that-specified-user-resources-must-be-allocated-to-the-project.}}

with the type of knowledge you expect that user to provide, on your user

\hypertarget{mandated-constraints}{%
\section{3. Mandated Constraints}\label{mandated-constraints}}

This section describes constraints on the eventual design of the
product.

Constraints are global---they are factors that apply to the entire
product. The product must be built within the stated constraints. Often
you know about the constraints, or they are mandated before the project
gets under way. They are probably determined by management and are worth
considering carefully---they restrict what you can do and so shape the
product. Constraints, like other types of requirements have a
description, rationale, and fit criterion, and generally are written in
the same format as functional and non-functional requirements.

\hypertarget{a.-solution-constraints}{%
\subsection{\texorpdfstring{3a. Solution Constraints
}{3a. Solution Constraints }}\label{a.-solution-constraints}}

\hypertarget{content-10}{%
\subsubsection{Content}\label{content-10}}

\hypertarget{this-specifies-constraints-on-the-way-that-the-problem-must-be-solved.-describe-the-mandated-technology-or-solution.-include-any-appropriate-version-numbers.-you-should-also-explain-the-reason-for-using-the-technology.}{%
\subsubsection{This specifies constraints on the way that the problem
must be solved. Describe the mandated technology or solution. Include
any appropriate version numbers. You should also explain the reason for
using the
technology.}\label{this-specifies-constraints-on-the-way-that-the-problem-must-be-solved.-describe-the-mandated-technology-or-solution.-include-any-appropriate-version-numbers.-you-should-also-explain-the-reason-for-using-the-technology.}}

\hypertarget{motivation-10}{%
\subsubsection{Motivation}\label{motivation-10}}

\hypertarget{to-identify-constraints-that-guide-the-final-product.-your-client-customer-or-user-may-have-design-preferences-or-only-certain-solutions-may-be-acceptable.-if-these-constraints-are-not-met-your-solution-is-not-acceptable.}{%
\subsubsection{To identify constraints that guide the final product.
Your client, customer, or user may have design preferences, or only
certain solutions may be acceptable. If these constraints are not met,
your solution is not
acceptable.}\label{to-identify-constraints-that-guide-the-final-product.-your-client-customer-or-user-may-have-design-preferences-or-only-certain-solutions-may-be-acceptable.-if-these-constraints-are-not-met-your-solution-is-not-acceptable.}}

\hypertarget{examples-2}{%
\subsubsection{Examples}\label{examples-2}}

\hypertarget{constraints-are-written-using-the-same-form-as-other-atomic-requirements-refer-to-the-requirements-snow-cardshell-for-the-attributes.-it-is-important-for-each-constraint-to-have-a-rationale-and-a-fit-criterion-as-they-help-to-expose-false-constraints-solutions-masquerading-as-constraints.-also-you-will-usually-find-that-a-constraint-affects-the-entire-product-rather-than-one-or-more-product-use-cases.}{%
\subsubsection{Constraints are written using the same form as other
atomic requirements (refer to the requirements snow card/shell for the
attributes). It is important for each constraint to have a rationale and
a fit criterion, as they help to expose false constraints (solutions
masquerading as constraints). Also, you will usually find that a
constraint affects the entire product rather than one or more product
use
cases.}\label{constraints-are-written-using-the-same-form-as-other-atomic-requirements-refer-to-the-requirements-snow-cardshell-for-the-attributes.-it-is-important-for-each-constraint-to-have-a-rationale-and-a-fit-criterion-as-they-help-to-expose-false-constraints-solutions-masquerading-as-constraints.-also-you-will-usually-find-that-a-constraint-affects-the-entire-product-rather-than-one-or-more-product-use-cases.}}

\hypertarget{section-2}{%
\subsubsection{}\label{section-2}}

\hypertarget{description-the-product-shall-use-the-current-two-way-radio-system-to-communicate-with-the-drivers-in-their-trucks.}{%
\subsubsection{Description: The product shall use the current two-way
radio system to communicate with the drivers in their
trucks.}\label{description-the-product-shall-use-the-current-two-way-radio-system-to-communicate-with-the-drivers-in-their-trucks.}}

\hypertarget{rationale-the-client-will-not-pay-for-a-new-radio-system-nor-are-any-other-means-of-communication-available-to-the-drivers.}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Rationale: The client will not pay for a
new radio system, nor are any other means of communication available to
the drivers.
}{Rationale: The client will not pay for a new radio system, nor are any other means of communication available to the drivers. }}\label{rationale-the-client-will-not-pay-for-a-new-radio-system-nor-are-any-other-means-of-communication-available-to-the-drivers.}}

\hypertarget{fit-criterion-all-signals-generated-by-the-product-shall-be-audible-and-understandable-by-all-drivers-via-their-two-way-radio-system.}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Fit criterion: All signals generated by
the product shall be audible and understandable by all drivers via their
two-way radio system.
}{Fit criterion: All signals generated by the product shall be audible and understandable by all drivers via their two-way radio system. }}\label{fit-criterion-all-signals-generated-by-the-product-shall-be-audible-and-understandable-by-all-drivers-via-their-two-way-radio-system.}}

\subsubsection{}\label{section-3}}

\hypertarget{description-the-product-shall-operate-using-windows-xp.}{%

not wish to change to a later version.
}{Rationale: The client uses XP and does not wish to change to a later version. }}\label{rationale-the-client-uses-xp-and-does-not-wish-to-change-to-a-later-version.}}

\hypertarget{fit-criterion-the-product-shall-be-approved-as-xp-compliant-by-the-ms-testing-group.}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Fit criterion: The product shall be
approved as XP compliant by the MS testing group.
}{Fit criterion: The product shall be approved as XP compliant by the MS testing group. }}\label{fit-criterion-the-product-shall-be-approved-as-xp-compliant-by-the-ms-testing-group.}}

\hypertarget{section-4}{%

\hypertarget{considerations-2}{%
\subsubsection{Considerations}\label{considerations-2}}

\hypertarget{we-want-to-define-the-boundaries-within-which-we-can-solve-the-problem.-be-careful-because-anyone-who-has-experience-with-or-exposure-to-a-piece-of-technology-tends-to-see-requirements-in-terms-of-that-technology.-this-tendency-leads-people-to-impose-solution-constraints-for-the-wrong-reason-making-it-very-easy-for-false-constraints-to-creep-into-a-specification.-the-solution-constraints-should-only-be-those-that-are-absolutely-non-negotiable.-in-other-words-however-you-solve-this-problem-you-must-use-this-particular-technology.-any-other-solution-would-be-unacceptable.}{%
\subsubsection{We want to define the boundaries within which we can
solve the problem. Be careful, because anyone who has experience with or
exposure to a piece of technology tends to see requirements in terms of
that technology. This tendency leads people to impose solution
constraints for the wrong reason, making it very easy for false
constraints to creep into a specification. The solution constraints
should only be those that are absolutely non-negotiable. In other words,
however you solve this problem, you must use this particular technology.
Any other solution would be
unacceptable.}\label{we-want-to-define-the-boundaries-within-which-we-can-solve-the-problem.-be-careful-because-anyone-who-has-experience-with-or-exposure-to-a-piece-of-technology-tends-to-see-requirements-in-terms-of-that-technology.-this-tendency-leads-people-to-impose-solution-constraints-for-the-wrong-reason-making-it-very-easy-for-false-constraints-to-creep-into-a-specification.-the-solution-constraints-should-only-be-those-that-are-absolutely-non-negotiable.-in-other-words-however-you-solve-this-problem-you-must-use-this-particular-technology.-any-other-solution-would-be-unacceptable.}}

\subsubsection{Form}\label{form-10}}

\hypertarget{include-the-constraint-requirements-as-a-specific-type-of-atomic-requirement-in-your-requirements-spreadsheet-or-database.-for-attributes-of-an-atomic-requirement-see-the-atomic-requirements-shell-example-at-the-start-of-this-template.-also-refer-to-article-on-atomic-requirements-at-httpwww.volere.co.uk}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Include the constraint requirements as a
specific type of atomic requirement in your requirements spreadsheet or
database. For attributes of an atomic requirement see the Atomic
Requirements Shell example at the start of this template. Also refer to
article on atomic requirements at
\href{http://www.volere.co.uk/}{http://www.volere.co.uk}}{Include the constraint requirements as a specific type of atomic requirement in your requirements spreadsheet or database. For attributes of an atomic requirement see the Atomic Requirements Shell example at the start of this template. Also refer to article on atomic requirements at http://www.volere.co.uk}}\label{include-the-constraint-requirements-as-a-specific-type-of-atomic-requirement-in-your-requirements-spreadsheet-or-database.-for-attributes-of-an-atomic-requirement-see-the-atomic-requirements-shell-example-at-the-start-of-this-template.-also-refer-to-article-on-atomic-requirements-at-httpwww.volere.co.uk}}

\hypertarget{form-11}{%
\subsubsection{Form}\label{form-11}}

\hypertarget{a-diagram-that-represents-each-hardware-and-software-componentsubcomponentdevicebuilding-block-that-will-be-used-to-implement-the-product.-the-particular-diagrams-that-you-use-depend-on-your-organization-and-your-projects-ways-of-working-the-important-issue-is-that-the-implementation-environment-is-unambiguously-understandable-by-the-people-who-have-to-make-decisions-about-how-the-functional-and-non-functional-requirements-will-be-implemented.-types-of-uml-diagrams-commonly-used-are-class-component-component-structure-deployment-package-diagrams.-there-are-many-other-home-grown-diagrams.}{%
\subsubsection{A diagram that represents each hardware and software
component/subcomponent/device/building block that will be used to
implement the product. The particular diagrams that you use depend on
your organization and your projects' ways of working, the important
issue is that the implementation environment is unambiguously
understandable by the people who have to make decisions about how the
functional and non-functional requirements will be implemented. Types of
UML diagrams commonly used are: Class, Component, Component Structure,
Deployment, Package diagrams. There are many other home-grown
diagrams.}\label{a-diagram-that-represents-each-hardware-and-software-componentsubcomponentdevicebuilding-block-that-will-be-used-to-implement-the-product.-the-particular-diagrams-that-you-use-depend-on-your-organization-and-your-projects-ways-of-working-the-important-issue-is-that-the-implementation-environment-is-unambiguously-understandable-by-the-people-who-have-to-make-decisions-about-how-the-functional-and-non-functional-requirements-will-be-implemented.-types-of-uml-diagrams-commonly-used-are-class-component-component-structure-deployment-package-diagrams.-there-are-many-other-home-grown-diagrams.}}

\hypertarget{form-12}{%
\subsubsection{Form}\label{form-12}}

\hypertarget{a-diagram-or-table-that-identifies-all-the-interfaces-between-the-product-to-be-built-and-other-adjacent-systems.-bear-in-mind-that-the-adjacent-systems-might-be-software-human-or-hardware.-some-adjacent-systems-are-within-your-organization-and-hence-potentially-more-easily-understood-and-perhaps-influenced.-other-adjacent-systems-are-outside-your-organization-and-might-be-difficult-if-not-impossible-to-influence.-a-product-scope-diagram-see-8a-for-an-example-is-often-used-to-define-interfaces-with-partner-or-collaborative-applications.}{%
\subsubsection{A diagram or table that identifies all the interfaces
between the product to be built and other adjacent systems. Bear in mind
that the adjacent systems might be software, human or hardware. Some
adjacent systems are within your organization and hence potentially more
easily understood and perhaps influenced. Other adjacent systems are
outside your organization and might be difficult if not impossible to
influence. A product scope diagram (see 8a for an example) is often used
to define interfaces with partner or collaborative
applications.}\label{a-diagram-or-table-that-identifies-all-the-interfaces-between-the-product-to-be-built-and-other-adjacent-systems.-bear-in-mind-that-the-adjacent-systems-might-be-software-human-or-hardware.-some-adjacent-systems-are-within-your-organization-and-hence-potentially-more-easily-understood-and-perhaps-influenced.-other-adjacent-systems-are-outside-your-organization-and-might-be-difficult-if-not-impossible-to-influence.-a-product-scope-diagram-see-8a-for-an-example-is-often-used-to-define-interfaces-with-partner-or-collaborative-applications.}}

\hypertarget{d.-off-the-shelf-software}{%
\subsection{3d. Off-the-Shelf
Software}\label{d.-off-the-shelf-software}}

\hypertarget{content-13}{%
\subsubsection{Content}\label{content-13}}

\hypertarget{this-describes-commercial-open-source-or-any-other-off-the-shelf-software-ots-that-must-be-used-to-implement-some-of-the-requirements-for-the-product.-it-could-also-apply-to-non-software-ots-components-such-as-hardware-or-any-other-commercial-product-that-is-intended-as-part-of-the-solution.}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{This describes commercial, open source,
or any other off-the-shelf software (OTS) that must be used to implement
some of the requirements for the product. It could also apply to
non-software OTS components such as hardware or any other commercial
product that is intended as part of the solution.
}{This describes commercial, open source, or any other off-the-shelf software (OTS) that must be used to implement some of the requirements for the product. It could also apply to non-software OTS components such as hardware or any other commercial product that is intended as part of the solution. }}\label{this-describes-commercial-open-source-or-any-other-off-the-shelf-software-ots-that-must-be-used-to-implement-some-of-the-requirements-for-the-product.-it-could-also-apply-to-non-software-ots-components-such-as-hardware-or-any-other-commercial-product-that-is-intended-as-part-of-the-solution.}}

\subsubsection{Motivation}\label{motivation-13}}

\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{To identify and describe existing
commercial, free, open source, or other products to be incorporated into
the eventual product. The characteristics, behaviour, and interfaces of
the package are design constraints.
}{To identify and describe existing commercial, free, open source, or other products to be incorporated into the eventual product. The characteristics, behaviour, and interfaces of the package are design constraints. }}\label{to-identify-and-describe-existing-commercial-free-open-source-or-other-products-to-be-incorporated-into-the-eventual-product.-the-characteristics-behaviour-and-interfaces-of-the-package-are-design-constraints.}}

\hypertarget{considerations-5}{%
\subsubsection{Considerations}\label{considerations-5}}

\hypertarget{when-gathering-requirements-you-may-discover-requirements-that-conflict-with-the-behaviour-and-characteristics-of-the-ots-software.-keep-in-mind-that-the-use-of-ots-software-was-mandated-before-the-full-extent-of-the-requirements-became-known.-in-light-of-your-discoveries-you-must-consider-whether-the-ots-product-is-a-viable-choice.-if-the-use-of-the-ots-software-is-not-negotiable-then-the-conflicting-requirements-must-be-discarded.}{%
\subsubsection{When gathering requirements, you may discover
requirements that conflict with the behaviour and characteristics of the
OTS software. Keep in mind that the use of OTS software was mandated
before the full extent of the requirements became known. In light of
your discoveries, you must consider whether the OTS product is a viable
choice. If the use of the OTS software is not negotiable, then the
conflicting requirements must be
discarded.}\label{when-gathering-requirements-you-may-discover-requirements-that-conflict-with-the-behaviour-and-characteristics-of-the-ots-software.-keep-in-mind-that-the-use-of-ots-software-was-mandated-before-the-full-extent-of-the-requirements-became-known.-in-light-of-your-discoveries-you-must-consider-whether-the-ots-product-is-a-viable-choice.-if-the-use-of-the-ots-software-is-not-negotiable-then-the-conflicting-requirements-must-be-discarded.}}

\hypertarget{note-that-your-strategy-for-discovering-requirements-is-affected-by-the-decision-to-use-ots-software.-in-this-situation-you-investigate-the-work-context-in-parallel-with-making-comparisons-with-the-capabilities-of-the-ots-product.-depending-on-the-comprehensibility-of-the-ots-software-you-might-be-able-to-discover-the-matches-or-mismatches-without-having-to-write-each-of-the-business-requirements-in-atomic-detail.-the-mismatches-are-the-requirements-that-you-will-need-to-specify-so-that-you-can-decide-whether-to-satisfy-them-by-either-modifying-the-ots-software-or-satisfying-the-requirement-in-another-way-or-modifying-the-business-requirements.}{%
\subsubsection{Note that your strategy for discovering requirements is
affected by the decision to use OTS software. In this situation you
investigate the work context in parallel with making comparisons with
the capabilities of the OTS product. Depending on the comprehensibility
of the OTS software, you might be able to discover the matches or
mismatches without having to write each of the business requirements in
atomic detail. The mismatches are the requirements that you will need to
specify so that you can decide whether to satisfy them by either
modifying the OTS software or satisfying the requirement in another way
or modifying the business
requirements.}\label{note-that-your-strategy-for-discovering-requirements-is-affected-by-the-decision-to-use-ots-software.-in-this-situation-you-investigate-the-work-context-in-parallel-with-making-comparisons-with-the-capabilities-of-the-ots-product.-depending-on-the-comprehensibility-of-the-ots-software-you-might-be-able-to-discover-the-matches-or-mismatches-without-having-to-write-each-of-the-business-requirements-in-atomic-detail.-the-mismatches-are-the-requirements-that-you-will-need-to-specify-so-that-you-can-decide-whether-to-satisfy-them-by-either-modifying-the-ots-software-or-satisfying-the-requirement-in-another-way-or-modifying-the-business-requirements.}}

\hypertarget{given-the-spate-of-lawsuits-in-the-software-arena-you-should-consider-whether-any-legal-implications-might-arise-from-your-use-of-ots.-you-can-cover-this-in-section-17.-legal-requirements.}{%
\subsubsection{Given the spate of lawsuits in the software arena, you
should consider whether any legal implications might arise from your use
of OTS. You can cover this in section 17. Legal
Requirements.}\label{given-the-spate-of-lawsuits-in-the-software-arena-you-should-consider-whether-any-legal-implications-might-arise-from-your-use-of-ots.-you-can-cover-this-in-section-17.-legal-requirements.}}

\hypertarget{form-13}{%
\subsubsection{Form}\label{form-13}}

\hypertarget{models-or-written-documentation-that-specifies-the-functional-and-non-functional-requirements-that-can-be-implemented-using-this-ots-software-product.-if-the-ots-product-has-a-well-structured-requirements-specification-and-systems-architecture-model-then-that-provides-you-with-the-basis-for-identifying-which-of-your-requirements-can-be-satisfied-by-the-product.-if-the-products-documentation-is-not-traceable-and-well-organized-then-you-will-need-to-do-more-detailed-work-on-your-own-requirements-until-you-find-a-level-at-which-you-can-map-your-requirements-to-the-ots-product.}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Models or written documentation that
specifies the functional and non-functional requirements that can be
implemented using this OTS software product. If the OTS product has a
well structured requirements specification and systems architecture
model then that provides you with the basis for identifying which of
your requirements can be satisfied by the product. If the product's
documentation is not traceable and well organized then you will need to
do more detailed work on your own requirements until you find a level at
which you can map your requirements to the OTS product.
}{Models or written documentation that specifies the functional and non-functional requirements that can be implemented using this OTS software product. If the OTS product has a well structured requirements specification and systems architecture model then that provides you with the basis for identifying which of your requirements can be satisfied by the product. If the product's documentation is not traceable and well organized then you will need to do more detailed work on your own requirements until you find a level at which you can map your requirements to the OTS product. }}\label{models-or-written-documentation-that-specifies-the-functional-and-non-functional-requirements-that-can-be-implemented-using-this-ots-software-product.-if-the-ots-product-has-a-well-structured-requirements-specification-and-systems-architecture-model-then-that-provides-you-with-the-basis-for-identifying-which-of-your-requirements-can-be-satisfied-by-the-product.-if-the-products-documentation-is-not-traceable-and-well-organized-then-you-will-need-to-do-more-detailed-work-on-your-own-requirements-until-you-find-a-level-at-which-you-can-map-your-requirements-to-the-ots-product.}}

\hypertarget{another-form-is-a-person-or-people-who-are-experts-in-the-ots-product-and-can-answer-your-questions-without-you-having-to-puzzle-through-cryptic-or-marketing-oriented-documents.}{%
\subsubsection{Another form is a person or people who are experts in the
OTS product and can answer your questions without you having to puzzle
through cryptic or marketing-oriented
documents.}\label{another-form-is-a-person-or-people-who-are-experts-in-the-ots-product-and-can-answer-your-questions-without-you-having-to-puzzle-through-cryptic-or-marketing-oriented-documents.}}

\hypertarget{e.-anticipated-workplace-environment}{%
\subsection{3e. Anticipated Workplace
Environment}\label{e.-anticipated-workplace-environment}}

\hypertarget{content-14}{%
\subsubsection{Content}\label{content-14}}

\hypertarget{this-describes-the-workplace-in-which-the-users-are-to-work-and-use-the-product.-it-should-describe-any-features-of-the-workplace-that-could-have-an-effect-on-the-design-of-the-product-and-the-social-and-cultural-aspects-of-the-workplace.}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{This describes the workplace in which the
users are to work and use the product. It should describe any features
of the workplace that could have an effect on the design of the product,
and the social and cultural aspects of the workplace.
}{This describes the workplace in which the users are to work and use the product. It should describe any features of the workplace that could have an effect on the design of the product, and the social and cultural aspects of the workplace. }}\label{this-describes-the-workplace-in-which-the-users-are-to-work-and-use-the-product.-it-should-describe-any-features-of-the-workplace-that-could-have-an-effect-on-the-design-of-the-product-and-the-social-and-cultural-aspects-of-the-workplace.}}

\subsubsection{The intention is to restrict the wildest ambitions and to
prevent the team from gathering requirements for an Airbus 380 when the
budget can buy only a Cessna. Is it realistic to build a product within
this budget? If the answer to this question is no, then either the
client is not really committed to building the product or the client
does not place enough value on the product. In either case you should
consider whether it is worthwhile
continuing.}\label{the-intention-is-to-restrict-the-wildest-ambitions-and-to-prevent-the-team-from-gathering-requirements-for-an-airbus-380-when-the-budget-can-buy-only-a-cessna.-is-it-realistic-to-build-a-product-within-this-budget-if-the-answer-to-this-question-is-no-then-either-the-client-is-not-really-committed-to-building-the-product-or-the-client-does-not-place-enough-value-on-the-product.-in-either-case-you-should-consider-whether-it-is-worthwhile-continuing.}}

that are outside the obvious boundary of your project scope.

\hypertarget{naming-conventions-and-terminology}{%
\section{\texorpdfstring{4. Naming Conventions and Terminology
}{4. Naming Conventions and Terminology }}\label{naming-conventions-and-terminology}}

It has been our experience that all projects have their own unique
vocabulary usually containing a variety of acronyms and abbreviations.
Failure to understand this project-specific nomenclature correctly
inevitably leads to misunderstandings, hours of lost time,
miscommunication between team members, and ultimately poor-quality
specifications.

\hypertarget{a.-definitions-of-all-terms-including-acronyms-used-by-stakeholders-involved-in-the-project}{%
\subsection{4a. Definitions of All Terms, Including Acronyms, Used by
Stakeholders Involved in the
Project}\label{a.-definitions-of-all-terms-including-acronyms-used-by-stakeholders-involved-in-the-project}}

\hypertarget{content-18}{%
\subsubsection{Content}\label{content-18}}

\hypertarget{a-glossary-containing-the-meanings-of-all-names-acronyms-and-abbreviations-used-by-the-stakeholders.-select-names-carefully-to-avoid-giving-a-different-unintended-meaning.}{%
\subsubsection{A glossary containing the meanings of all names,
acronyms, and abbreviations used by the stakeholders. Select names
carefully to avoid giving a different, unintended
meaning.}\label{a-glossary-containing-the-meanings-of-all-names-acronyms-and-abbreviations-used-by-the-stakeholders.-select-names-carefully-to-avoid-giving-a-different-unintended-meaning.}}

\hypertarget{if-the-work-that-you-are-studying-already-has-a-glossary-of-terms-then-use-this-as-your-starting-point.-this-glossary-should-be-enlarged-and-refined-as-the-analysis-proceeds-but-for-the-moment-it-should-introduce-the-terms-that-the-stakeholders-use-and-the-meanings-of-those-terms.this-glossary-reflects-the-terminology-in-current-use-within-the-work-area.-you-might-also-get-started-by-building-on-the-standard-names-used-within-your-industry.}{%
\subsubsection{If the work that you are studying already has a glossary
of terms then use this as your starting point. This glossary should be
enlarged and refined as the analysis proceeds, but for the moment, it
should introduce the terms that the stakeholders use and the meanings of
those terms.This glossary reflects the terminology in current use within
the work area. You might also get started by building on the standard
names used within your
industry.}\label{if-the-work-that-you-are-studying-already-has-a-glossary-of-terms-then-use-this-as-your-starting-point.-this-glossary-should-be-enlarged-and-refined-as-the-analysis-proceeds-but-for-the-moment-it-should-introduce-the-terms-that-the-stakeholders-use-and-the-meanings-of-those-terms.this-glossary-reflects-the-terminology-in-current-use-within-the-work-area.-you-might-also-get-started-by-building-on-the-standard-names-used-within-your-industry.}}

\hypertarget{for-each-term-write-a-description.-the-appropriate-stakeholders-must-agree-on-this-description-of-the-meaning-of-the-term.}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{For each term, write a description. The
appropriate stakeholders must agree on this description of the meaning
of the term.
}{For each term, write a description. The appropriate stakeholders must agree on this description of the meaning of the term. }}\label{for-each-term-write-a-description.-the-appropriate-stakeholders-must-agree-on-this-description-of-the-meaning-of-the-term.}}

\hypertarget{we-suggest-you-add-all-acronyms-and-abbreviations.-we-often-encounter-situations-where-team-members-use-acronyms-but-admit-they-do-not-know-the-meanings-of-those-acronyms.-this-section-gives-you-a-place-to-register-your-acronyms.}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{We suggest you add \emph{all} acronyms
and abbreviations. We often encounter situations where team members use
acronyms, but admit they do not know the meanings of those acronyms.
This section gives you a place to register your acronyms.
}{We suggest you add all acronyms and abbreviations. We often encounter situations where team members use acronyms, but admit they do not know the meanings of those acronyms. This section gives you a place to register your acronyms. }}\label{we-suggest-you-add-all-acronyms-and-abbreviations.-we-often-encounter-situations-where-team-members-use-acronyms-but-admit-they-do-not-know-the-meanings-of-those-acronyms.-this-section-gives-you-a-place-to-register-your-acronyms.}}

\hypertarget{motivation-18}{%
\subsubsection{Motivation}\label{motivation-18}}

\hypertarget{names-are-very-important.-they-invoke-meanings-that-if-carefully-defined-can-save-hours-of-explanations.-attention-to-names-early-in-the-project-helps-to-highlight-misunderstandings.}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Names are very important. They invoke
meanings that, if carefully defined, can save hours of explanations.
Attention to names early in the project helps to highlight
misunderstandings.
}{Names are very important. They invoke meanings that, if carefully defined, can save hours of explanations. Attention to names early in the project helps to highlight misunderstandings. }}\label{names-are-very-important.-they-invoke-meanings-that-if-carefully-defined-can-save-hours-of-explanations.-attention-to-names-early-in-the-project-helps-to-highlight-misunderstandings.}}

\hypertarget{as-the-detailed-work-progresses-the-glossary-provides-input-to-the-more-precisely-specified-businesswork-data-model-and-data-dictionary-see-section-7-of-the-template.-as-the-analysis-data-dictionary-evolves-many-of-the-definitions-from-the-glossary-are-expanded-in-the-dictionary-by-adding-their-data-composition.}{%
\subsubsection{As the detailed work progresses the glossary provides
input to the more precisely specified business/work data model and data
dictionary -- see section 7 of the template. As the analysis data
dictionary evolves, many of the definitions from the glossary are
expanded in the dictionary by adding their data
composition.}\label{as-the-detailed-work-progresses-the-glossary-provides-input-to-the-more-precisely-specified-businesswork-data-model-and-data-dictionary-see-section-7-of-the-template.-as-the-analysis-data-dictionary-evolves-many-of-the-definitions-from-the-glossary-are-expanded-in-the-dictionary-by-adding-their-data-composition.}}

\hypertarget{relevant-facts-and-assumptions}{%
\section{5. Relevant Facts and
Assumptions}\label{relevant-facts-and-assumptions}}

Relevant facts are external factors that have an effect on the product
but are not covered by other sections in the requirements template. They
are not necessarily translated into requirements but could be. Relevant
facts alert the developers to conditions and factors that have a bearing
on the requirements.

\hypertarget{a.-relevant-facts}{%
\subsection{5a. Relevant Facts}\label{a.-relevant-facts}}

\hypertarget{content-19}{%
\subsubsection{Content}\label{content-19}}

\hypertarget{factors-that-have-an-effect-on-the-product-but-are-not-mandated-requirements-constraints.-facts-provide-the-reader-of-the-specification-with-more-background-for-understanding-the-business-problem.}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Factors that have an effect on the
product, but are not mandated requirements constraints. Facts provide
the reader of the specification with more background for understanding
the business problem.
}{Factors that have an effect on the product, but are not mandated requirements constraints. Facts provide the reader of the specification with more background for understanding the business problem. }}\label{factors-that-have-an-effect-on-the-product-but-are-not-mandated-requirements-constraints.-facts-provide-the-reader-of-the-specification-with-more-background-for-understanding-the-business-problem.}}

\hypertarget{motivation-19}{%
\subsubsection{Motivation}\label{motivation-19}}

\hypertarget{relevant-facts-provide-background-information-to-the-specification-readers-and-might-contribute-to-requirements.-they-will-have-an-effect-on-the-eventual-design-of-the-product.}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Relevant facts provide background
information to the specification readers, and might contribute to
requirements. They will have an effect on the eventual design of the
product.
}{Relevant facts provide background information to the specification readers, and might contribute to requirements. They will have an effect on the eventual design of the product. }}\label{relevant-facts-provide-background-information-to-the-specification-readers-and-might-contribute-to-requirements.-they-will-have-an-effect-on-the-eventual-design-of-the-product.}}

revisit them and use them as triggers to discover relevant requirements.

It is often difficult to immediately ascertain whether a business rule is or is not relevant to the project that you are doing. This section provides a place to capture the business rules and, as understanding of the work increases, to revisit them and use them as triggers to discover relevant requirements. }}\label{business-rules-are-mentioned-at-all-stages-of-the-requirements-discovery-process.-it-is-often-difficult-to-immediately-ascertain-whether-a-business-rule-is-or-is-not-relevant-to-the-project-that-you-are-doing.-this-section-provides-a-place-to-capture-the-business-rules-and-as-understanding-of-the-work-increases-to-revisit-them-and-use-them-as-triggers-to-discover-relevant-requirements.}}

\hypertarget{the-assumptions-are-intended-to-be-transient.-that-is-they-should-all-be-cleared-by-the-time-the-specification-is-releasedthe-assumption-should-have-become-either-a-requirement-or-a-constraint.-for-example-if-the-assumption-related-to-the-capability-of-a-product-that-is-intended-to-be-a-partner-product-to-yours-then-the-capability-should-have-been-proven-satisfactory-and-it-becomes-a-constraint-to-use-it.-conversely-if-the-bought-in-product-is-not-suitable-then-it-becomes-a-requirement-for-the-project-team-to-construct-the-needed-capability.}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{The assumptions are intended to be
transient. That is, they should all be cleared by the time the
specification is released---the assumption should have become either a
requirement or a constraint. For example, if the assumption related to
the capability of a product that is intended to be a partner product to
yours, then the capability should have been proven satisfactory, and it
becomes a constraint to use it. Conversely, if the bought-in product is
not suitable, then it becomes a requirement for the project team to
construct the needed capability.
}{The assumptions are intended to be transient. That is, they should all be cleared by the time the specification is released---the assumption should have become either a requirement or a constraint. For example, if the assumption related to the capability of a product that is intended to be a partner product to yours, then the capability should have been proven satisfactory, and it becomes a constraint to use it. Conversely, if the bought-in product is not suitable, then it becomes a requirement for the project team to construct the needed capability. }}\label{the-assumptions-are-intended-to-be-transient.-that-is-they-should-all-be-cleared-by-the-time-the-specification-is-releasedthe-assumption-should-have-become-either-a-requirement-or-a-constraint.-for-example-if-the-assumption-related-to-the-capability-of-a-product-that-is-intended-to-be-a-partner-product-to-yours-then-the-capability-should-have-been-proven-satisfactory-and-it-becomes-a-constraint-to-use-it.-conversely-if-the-bought-in-product-is-not-suitable-then-it-becomes-a-requirement-for-the-project-team-to-construct-the-needed-capability.}}

\hypertarget{form-19}{%
\subsubsection{Form}\label{form-19}}

\hypertarget{a-written-statement-describing-the-assumption-along-with-the-effect-on-the-project-if-the-assumption-is-false.-depending-on-the-complexity-of-the-assumption-it-might-be-necessary-to-include-references-to-other-documents-or-people}{%
\subsubsection{A written statement describing the assumption along with
the effect on the project if the assumption is false. Depending on the
complexity of the assumption, it might be necessary to include
references to other documents or
people}\label{a-written-statement-describing-the-assumption-along-with-the-effect-on-the-project-if-the-assumption-is-false.-depending-on-the-complexity-of-the-assumption-it-might-be-necessary-to-include-references-to-other-documents-or-people}}

\hypertarget{understanding-of-assumptions-can-be-explored-and-shared-by-using-cause-and-effect-diagrams-such-as-peter-senges-dynamics-models.}{%
\subsubsection{Understanding of assumptions can be explored and shared
by using cause and effect diagrams such as Peter Senge's dynamics
models.}\label{understanding-of-assumptions-can-be-explored-and-shared-by-using-cause-and-effect-diagrams-such-as-peter-senges-dynamics-models.}}

\hypertarget{the-scope-of-the-work}{%
\section{6. The Scope of the Work}\label{the-scope-of-the-work}}

The scope of the work determines the boundaries of the business area to
be studied and outlines how it fits into its environment. Once you
understand the work and its constraints, you can establish the scope of
the product see Section 8 of the template.

\hypertarget{a.-the-current-situation}{%
\subsection{6a. The Current Situation}\label{a.-the-current-situation}}

\hypertarget{content-22}{%
\subsubsection{Content}\label{content-22}}

\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{This is an analysis of the existing
business processes, including the manual and automated processes that
might be replaced or changed by the new product. In terms of the Volere
Brown Cow model you refer to this view as the ``How Now'' view. Business
analysts might already have done this investigation as part of the
business case analysis for the project. This is where it might be
appropriate to build some Business process models. These are models of
the processes that the business uses to carry out the work of the
organization. The models include roles, individuals, departments,
technology and procedures. They illustrate the workflow and the
dependencies between the components of the process.

\hypertarget{motivation-22}{%
\subsubsection{Motivation}\label{motivation-22}}

\hypertarget{if-your-project-intends-to-make-changes-to-an-existing-manual-or-automated-system-you-need-to-understand-the-effect-of-proposed-changes.-the-study-of-the-current-situation-provides-the-basis-for-understanding-the-effects-of-proposed-changes-and-choosing-the-best-alternatives.-business-process-modelling-does-not-always-lead-to-building-software.-instead-some-changes-in-procedures-and-the-way-roles-are-allocated-might-be-the-best-way-of-making-a-necessary-improvement.}{%
\subsubsection{If your project intends to make changes to an existing
manual or automated system, you need to understand the effect of
proposed changes. The study of the current situation provides the basis
for understanding the effects of proposed changes and choosing the best
alternatives. Business process modelling does not always lead to
building software. Instead, some changes in procedures and the way roles
are allocated might be the best way of making a necessary
improvement.}\label{if-your-project-intends-to-make-changes-to-an-existing-manual-or-automated-system-you-need-to-understand-the-effect-of-proposed-changes.-the-study-of-the-current-situation-provides-the-basis-for-understanding-the-effects-of-proposed-changes-and-choosing-the-best-alternatives.-business-process-modelling-does-not-always-lead-to-building-software.-instead-some-changes-in-procedures-and-the-way-roles-are-allocated-might-be-the-best-way-of-making-a-necessary-improvement.}}

\hypertarget{b.-the-context-of-the-work}{%
\subsection{6b. The Context of the
Work}\label{b.-the-context-of-the-work}}

\hypertarget{content-23}{%
\subsubsection{Content}\label{content-23}}

\hypertarget{the-work-context-diagram-identifies-the-boundaries-of-the-work-that-you-need-to-investigate-to-be-able-to-build-the-product.-note-that-it-includes-more-than-the-intended-product.-unless-you-understand-the-work-that-the-product-will-support-you-have-little-chance-of-building-a-product-that-will-fit-cleanly-into-its-environment.}{%
\subsubsection{The work context diagram identifies the boundaries of the
work that you need to investigate to be able to build the product. Note
that it includes more than the intended product. Unless you understand
the work that the product will support, you have little chance of
building a product that will fit cleanly into its
environment.}\label{the-work-context-diagram-identifies-the-boundaries-of-the-work-that-you-need-to-investigate-to-be-able-to-build-the-product.-note-that-it-includes-more-than-the-intended-product.-unless-you-understand-the-work-that-the-product-will-support-you-have-little-chance-of-building-a-product-that-will-fit-cleanly-into-its-environment.}}

\hypertarget{the-adjacent-systems-on-the-example-context-diagram-e.g.-weather-forecasting-service-indicate-other-subject-matter-domains-systems-people-and-organizations-that-need-to-be-understood.-the-interfaces-between-the-adjacent-systems-and-the-work-context-indicate-why-we-are-interested-in-the-adjacent-system.-in-the-case-of-weather-forecasting-service-we-can-say-that-we-are-interested-in-the-details-of-when-how-where-who-what-and-why-it-produces-the-district-weather-forecasts-information.}{%
\subsubsection{The adjacent systems on the example context diagram
(e.g., Weather Forecasting Service) indicate other subject matter
domains (systems, people, and organizations) that need to be understood.
The interfaces between the adjacent systems and the work context
indicate why we are interested in the adjacent system. In the case of
Weather Forecasting Service, we can say that we are interested in the
details of when, how, where, who, what, and why it produces the District
Weather Forecasts
information.}\label{the-adjacent-systems-on-the-example-context-diagram-e.g.-weather-forecasting-service-indicate-other-subject-matter-domains-systems-people-and-organizations-that-need-to-be-understood.-the-interfaces-between-the-adjacent-systems-and-the-work-context-indicate-why-we-are-interested-in-the-adjacent-system.-in-the-case-of-weather-forecasting-service-we-can-say-that-we-are-interested-in-the-details-of-when-how-where-who-what-and-why-it-produces-the-district-weather-forecasts-information.}}

and hence the requirements effort. Without this definition, we have

\hypertarget{content-24}{%
\subsubsection{Content}\label{content-24}}

\hypertarget{a-list-showing-all-business-events-to-which-the-work-responds.-business-events-are-happenings-in-the-real-world-that-affect-the-work.-they-also-happen-because-it-is-time-for-the-work-to-do-somethingfor-example-produce-weekly-reports-remind-non-paying-customers-check-the-status-of-a-device-and-so-on.-the-response-to-each-event-is-called-a-business-use-case-known-as-a-buc-it-represents-a-discrete-partition-of-work-that-contributes-to-the-total-functionality-of-the-work.}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{A list showing all business events to
which the work responds. Business events are happenings in the real
world that affect the work. They also happen because it is time for the
work to do something---for example, produce weekly reports, remind
non-paying customers, check the status of a device, and so on. The
response to each event is called a business use case (known as a BUC);
it represents a discrete partition of work that contributes to the total
functionality of the work.
}{A list showing all business events to which the work responds. Business events are happenings in the real world that affect the work. They also happen because it is time for the work to do something---for example, produce weekly reports, remind non-paying customers, check the status of a device, and so on. The response to each event is called a business use case (known as a BUC); it represents a discrete partition of work that contributes to the total functionality of the work. }}\label{a-list-showing-all-business-events-to-which-the-work-responds.-business-events-are-happenings-in-the-real-world-that-affect-the-work.-they-also-happen-because-it-is-time-for-the-work-to-do-somethingfor-example-produce-weekly-reports-remind-non-paying-customers-check-the-status-of-a-device-and-so-on.-the-response-to-each-event-is-called-a-business-use-case-known-as-a-buc-it-represents-a-discrete-partition-of-work-that-contributes-to-the-total-functionality-of-the-work.}}
