\hypertarget{motivation-24}{%
\subsubsection{Motivation}\label{motivation-24}}

\hypertarget{to-identify-logical-chunks-of-the-work-that-can-be-used-as-the-basis-for-discovering-detailed-requirements.-these-business-events-also-provide-the-subsystems-that-can-be-used-as-the-basis-for-managing-detailed-analysis-and-design.-each-business-event-has-a-business-use-case-buc-whose-details-can-be-studied-independently.-however-all-bucs-connect-to-each-other-through-the-stored-business-data-see-section-7.}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{To identify logical chunks of the work
that can be used as the basis for discovering detailed requirements.
These business events also provide the subsystems that can be used as
the basis for managing detailed analysis and design. Each business event
has a business use case (BUC) whose details can be studied
independently. However all BUCs connect to each other through the stored
business data (see section 7).\\
}{To identify logical chunks of the work that can be used as the basis for discovering detailed requirements. These business events also provide the subsystems that can be used as the basis for managing detailed analysis and design. Each business event has a business use case (BUC) whose details can be studied independently. However all BUCs connect to each other through the stored business data (see section 7). }}\label{to-identify-logical-chunks-of-the-work-that-can-be-used-as-the-basis-for-discovering-detailed-requirements.-these-business-events-also-provide-the-subsystems-that-can-be-used-as-the-basis-for-managing-detailed-analysis-and-design.-each-business-event-has-a-business-use-case-buc-whose-details-can-be-studied-independently.-however-all-bucs-connect-to-each-other-through-the-stored-business-data-see-section-7.}}

\hypertarget{example}{%
\subsubsection{Example}\label{example}}

Business Event List

Event Name Input and Output Summary of BUC

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.3340}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2924}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\columnwidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.3736}}@{}}
\toprule()
\endhead
1. Weather Station transmits reading & Weather Station Readings (in) &
Record the readings as belonging to the weather station. \\
2. Weather Service forecasts weather & District Weather Forecast (in) &
Record the forecast. \\
3. Road engineers advise changed roads & Changed Road (in) & Record the
new or changed road. Check that all appropriate weather stations are
attached. \\
4. Road Engineering installs new Weather Station & New Weather Station
(in) & Record the weather station and attach it to the appropriate
roads. \\
5. Road Engineering changes Weather Station & Changed Weather Station
(in) & Record the changes to the weather station. \\
6. Time to test Weather Stations & Failed Weather Station Alert (out) &
Determine if any weather stations have not transmitted for two hours,
and inform Road Engineering of any failures. \\
7. Truck Depot changes a truck & Truck Change (in) & Record the changes
to the truck. \\
8. Time to detect icy roads & Road De-icing Schedule (out) & Predict the
ice situation for the next two hours. Assign a truck to any roads that
will freeze. Issue the schedule. \\
9. Truck treats a road & Treated Road (in) & Record the road as being in
a safe condition for the next three hours. \\
10 Truck Depot reports problem with truck & Truck Breakdown (in)

Amended Gritting Schedule (out) & Reassign available trucks to the
previously assigned roads. \\
11. Time to monitor road treatment & Untreated Road Reminder (out) &
Check that all scheduled roads have been treated in the assigned time,
and issue reminders for any untreated roads. \\
& & \\
\bottomrule()
\end{longtable}

\hypertarget{considerations-13}{%
\subsubsection{Considerations}\label{considerations-13}}

\hypertarget{attempting-to-list-the-business-events-and-do-a-one-sentence-summary-of-each-of-the-bucs-is-a-way-of-testing-the-work-context.-this-activity-uncovers-uncertainties-and-misunderstandings-about-the-project-and-facilitates-precise-communications.-when-you-do-an-event-analysis-it-will-usually-prompt-you-to-make-some-changes-to-your-work-context-diagram.}{%
\subsubsection{Attempting to list the business events and do a
one-sentence summary of each of the BUCs is a way of testing the work
context. This activity uncovers uncertainties and misunderstandings
about the project and facilitates precise communications. When you do an
event analysis, it will usually prompt you to make some changes to your
work context
diagram.}\label{attempting-to-list-the-business-events-and-do-a-one-sentence-summary-of-each-of-the-bucs-is-a-way-of-testing-the-work-context.-this-activity-uncovers-uncertainties-and-misunderstandings-about-the-project-and-facilitates-precise-communications.-when-you-do-an-event-analysis-it-will-usually-prompt-you-to-make-some-changes-to-your-work-context-diagram.}}

\hypertarget{we-suggest-you-gather-requirements-for-discrete-sections-of-the-work.-this-requires-you-to-partition-the-work-and-we-have-found-business-events-to-be-the-most-convenient-consistent-and-natural-way-to-break-the-work-into-manageable-units-and-to-be-able-to-trace-the-details-back-to-the-scope-of-the-work.}{%
\subsubsection{We suggest you gather requirements for discrete sections
of the work. This requires you to partition the work, and we have found
business events to be the most convenient, consistent, and natural way
to break the work into manageable units and to be able to trace the
details back to the scope of the
work.}\label{we-suggest-you-gather-requirements-for-discrete-sections-of-the-work.-this-requires-you-to-partition-the-work-and-we-have-found-business-events-to-be-the-most-convenient-consistent-and-natural-way-to-break-the-work-into-manageable-units-and-to-be-able-to-trace-the-details-back-to-the-scope-of-the-work.}}

\hypertarget{form-22}{%
\subsubsection{Form}\label{form-22}}

\hypertarget{business-event-listtable-containing-for-each-event-event-number-event-name-name-of-input-name-of-outputs-summary-of-the-business-event-response.-the-names-on-the-business-event-list-must-match-the-names-on-the-work-context-modeltable-ref.-6.b}{%
\subsubsection{Business event list/table containing for each event:
Event number, Event name, Name of input, Name of output/s, Summary of
the business event response. The names on the business event list must
match the names on the work context model/table ref.
6.b}\label{business-event-listtable-containing-for-each-event-event-number-event-name-name-of-input-name-of-outputs-summary-of-the-business-event-response.-the-names-on-the-business-event-list-must-match-the-names-on-the-work-context-modeltable-ref.-6.b}}

\hypertarget{d.-specifying-a-business-use-case-buc}{%
\subsection{6d. Specifying a Business Use Case
(BUC)}\label{d.-specifying-a-business-use-case-buc}}

\hypertarget{content-25}{%
\subsubsection{Content}\label{content-25}}

\hypertarget{a-specification-of-the-details-of-how-a-business-use-case-buc-responds-to-a-business-event.}{%
\subsubsection{A specification of the details of how a Business Use Case
(BUC) responds to a Business
Event.}\label{a-specification-of-the-details-of-how-a-business-use-case-buc-responds-to-a-business-event.}}

\hypertarget{motivation-25}{%
\subsubsection{Motivation}\label{motivation-25}}

\hypertarget{to-understand-the-detailed-business-response-that-must-be-carried-out-when-a-business-event-takes-place-and-provide-a-basis-for-discovering-the-detailed-requirements.-the-understanding-of-the-buc-also-provides-the-basis-for-discussing-which-parts-of-the-buc-should-be-carried-out-by-the-product-that-will-be-built.}{%
\subsubsection{To understand the detailed business response that must be
carried out when a business event takes place and provide a basis for
discovering the detailed requirements. The understanding of the BUC also
provides the basis for discussing which parts of the BUC should be
carried out by the product that will be
built.}\label{to-understand-the-detailed-business-response-that-must-be-carried-out-when-a-business-event-takes-place-and-provide-a-basis-for-discovering-the-detailed-requirements.-the-understanding-of-the-buc-also-provides-the-basis-for-discussing-which-parts-of-the-buc-should-be-carried-out-by-the-product-that-will-be-built.}}

\hypertarget{example-1}{%
\subsubsection{Example}\label{example-1}}

\hypertarget{in-the-sample-specifications-included-with-the-download-of-this-template-you-will-find-examples-of-buc-scenarios.}{%
\subsubsection{In the sample specifications included with the download
of this template you will find examples of BUC
scenarios.}\label{in-the-sample-specifications-included-with-the-download-of-this-template-you-will-find-examples-of-buc-scenarios.}}

\hypertarget{considerations-14}{%
\subsubsection{Considerations}\label{considerations-14}}

\hypertarget{whatever-approach-you-use-to-specify-the-details-of-a-buc-you-should-stay-within-the-boundary-of-the-input-and-outputs-for-that-business-event.-if-you-discover-additional-input-or-output-data-then-it-is-an-indication-that-you-need-to-make-changes-to-the-inputoutput-data-on-the-event-list-and-also-on-the-work-context-diagram.}{%
\subsubsection{Whatever approach you use to specify the details of a
BUC, you should stay within the boundary of the input and output/s for
that business event. If you discover additional input or output data
then it is an indication that you need to make changes to the
input/output data on the event list and also on the work context
diagram.}\label{whatever-approach-you-use-to-specify-the-details-of-a-buc-you-should-stay-within-the-boundary-of-the-input-and-outputs-for-that-business-event.-if-you-discover-additional-input-or-output-data-then-it-is-an-indication-that-you-need-to-make-changes-to-the-inputoutput-data-on-the-event-list-and-also-on-the-work-context-diagram.}}

\hypertarget{form-23}{%
\subsubsection{Form}\label{form-23}}

\hypertarget{a-buc-can-be-specified-using-any-combination-of-models-that-suits-the-analyst.-the-most-common-approaches-are-activity-diagrams-buc-scenarios-process-flow-diagrams-sequence-diagrams-mind-maps-interview-notes....-the-only-caveat-is-that-the-inputs-and-outputs-on-your-buc-are-precisely-the-same-and-hence-traceable-to-the-inputs-and-outputs-on-the-corresponding-business-event.}{%
\subsubsection{A BUC can be specified using any combination of models
that suits the analyst. The most common approaches are: activity
diagrams, BUC scenarios, process flow diagrams, sequence diagrams, mind
maps, interview notes.... The only caveat is that the inputs and outputs
on your BUC are precisely the same and hence traceable to the inputs and
outputs on the corresponding Business
Event.}\label{a-buc-can-be-specified-using-any-combination-of-models-that-suits-the-analyst.-the-most-common-approaches-are-activity-diagrams-buc-scenarios-process-flow-diagrams-sequence-diagrams-mind-maps-interview-notes....-the-only-caveat-is-that-the-inputs-and-outputs-on-your-buc-are-precisely-the-same-and-hence-traceable-to-the-inputs-and-outputs-on-the-corresponding-business-event.}}

\subsubsection{}\label{section-7}}

\hypertarget{business-data-model-and-data-dictionary}{%
\section{\texorpdfstring{7. Business Data Model and Data Dictionary
}{7. Business Data Model and Data Dictionary }}\label{business-data-model-and-data-dictionary}}

\hypertarget{a.-business-data-model}{%
\subsection{7a. Business Data Model}\label{a.-business-data-model}}

\hypertarget{content-26}{%
\subsubsection{Content}\label{content-26}}

\hypertarget{a-specification-of-the-essential-subject-matter-business-objects-entities-and-classes-that-are-germane-to-the-product.-it-might-take-the-form-of-a-first-cut-class-model-an-entity-relationship-model-or-any-other-kind-of-data-model.}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{A specification of the essential subject
matter, business objects, entities, and classes that are germane to the
product. It might take the form of a first-cut class model, an
entity-relationship model, or any other kind of data model.
}{A specification of the essential subject matter, business objects, entities, and classes that are germane to the product. It might take the form of a first-cut class model, an entity-relationship model, or any other kind of data model. }}\label{a-specification-of-the-essential-subject-matter-business-objects-entities-and-classes-that-are-germane-to-the-product.-it-might-take-the-form-of-a-first-cut-class-model-an-entity-relationship-model-or-any-other-kind-of-data-model.}}

\hypertarget{motivation-26}{%
\subsubsection{Motivation}\label{motivation-26}}

\hypertarget{to-clarify-the-systems-subject-matter-thereby-triggering-recognition-of-requirements-not-yet-considered.-to-discover-missing-requirements-you-can-cross-check-the-data-model-and-the-events-using-a-create-reference-update-delete-crud-table.-the-data-model-is-a-specification-for-all-of-the-business-data-that-is-relevant-to-the-scope-of-the-work.}{%
\subsubsection{To clarify the system's subject matter, thereby
triggering recognition of requirements not yet considered. To discover
missing requirements you can cross check the data model and the events
using a Create, Reference, Update, Delete (CRUD) table. The data model
is a specification for all of the business data that is relevant to the
scope of the
work.}\label{to-clarify-the-systems-subject-matter-thereby-triggering-recognition-of-requirements-not-yet-considered.-to-discover-missing-requirements-you-can-cross-check-the-data-model-and-the-events-using-a-create-reference-update-delete-crud-table.-the-data-model-is-a-specification-for-all-of-the-business-data-that-is-relevant-to-the-scope-of-the-work.}}

\hypertarget{example-2}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Example }{Example }}\label{example-2}}

\hypertarget{this-is-a-model-of-the-business-systems-business-subject-matter-using-the-unified-modelling-language-uml-class-model-notation.-this-is-all-the-data-that-is-created-referenced-updated-and-deleted-by-processes-within-the-scope-of-the-work-being-studied.-see-section-6-for-more-about-the-scope-of-the-work.}{%
\subsubsection{This is a model of the business system's business subject
matter using the Unified Modelling Language (UML) class model notation.
This is all the data that is Created, Referenced, Updated and Deleted by
processes within the scope of the work being studied. See section 6 for
more about the scope of the
work.}\label{this-is-a-model-of-the-business-systems-business-subject-matter-using-the-unified-modelling-language-uml-class-model-notation.-this-is-all-the-data-that-is-created-referenced-updated-and-deleted-by-processes-within-the-scope-of-the-work-being-studied.-see-section-6-for-more-about-the-scope-of-the-work.}}

\hypertarget{if-your-organization-prefers-a-particular-model-then-you-must-use-that-one.-the-important-thing-is-that-the-data-model-that-you-build-is-a-business-data-model-not-a-design-for-a-database.-your-model-is-concerned-with-identifying-business-classes-by-making-a-logical-partitioning-of-all-the-data-within-the-work-context-and-the-necessary-business-relationships-between-those-business-classes.-your-model-is-used-as-input-to-designing-how-the-data-will-be-implemented.-the-definitions-of-the-attributes-in-each-business-class-is-in-the-data-dictionary-see-section-7b.}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{If your organization prefers a particular
model then you must use that one. The important thing is that the data
model that you build is a \emph{business data model,} not a design for a
database. Your model is concerned with identifying business classes by
making a logical partitioning of all the data within the work context
and the necessary business relationships between those business classes.
Your model is used as input to designing how the data will be
implemented. The definitions of the attributes in each business class is
in the data dictionary (see section
7b).}{If your organization prefers a particular model then you must use that one. The important thing is that the data model that you build is a business data model, not a design for a database. Your model is concerned with identifying business classes by making a logical partitioning of all the data within the work context and the necessary business relationships between those business classes. Your model is used as input to designing how the data will be implemented. The definitions of the attributes in each business class is in the data dictionary (see section 7b).}}\label{if-your-organization-prefers-a-particular-model-then-you-must-use-that-one.-the-important-thing-is-that-the-data-model-that-you-build-is-a-business-data-model-not-a-design-for-a-database.-your-model-is-concerned-with-identifying-business-classes-by-making-a-logical-partitioning-of-all-the-data-within-the-work-context-and-the-necessary-business-relationships-between-those-business-classes.-your-model-is-used-as-input-to-designing-how-the-data-will-be-implemented.-the-definitions-of-the-attributes-in-each-business-class-is-in-the-data-dictionary-see-section-7b.}}

\hypertarget{b.-data-dictionary}{%
\subsection{7b. Data Dictionary}\label{b.-data-dictionary}}

The glossary described earlier in section 4 of the template is the
starting point for establishing common understanding of terminology. As
you start to define the scope of the investigation you define the data
inputs and outputs in a formal data dictionary. The terms that you
define in this dictionary, right down to elemental level, are the same
terms that you use when defining detailed atomic requirements.

\hypertarget{content-27}{%
\subsubsection{Content}\label{content-27}}

\hypertarget{the-data-dictionary-specifies-the-content-of}{%
\subsubsection{The data dictionary specifies the content
of:}\label{the-data-dictionary-specifies-the-content-of}}

\begin{itemize}
\item ~
  \hypertarget{classes-on-the-data-model}{%
  \subsubsection{Classes on the data
  model}\label{classes-on-the-data-model}}
\item ~
  \hypertarget{attributes-of-the-classes}{%
  \subsubsection{Attributes of the
  classes}\label{attributes-of-the-classes}}
\item ~
  \hypertarget{relationships-between-the-classes}{%
  \subsubsection{Relationships between the
  classes}\label{relationships-between-the-classes}}
\item ~
  \hypertarget{inputs-and-outputs-on-all-models}{%
  \subsubsection{Inputs and Outputs on all
  models}\label{inputs-and-outputs-on-all-models}}
\item ~
  \hypertarget{elements-of-data-within-the-inputs-and-outputs}{%
  \subsubsection{Elements of data within the Inputs and
  Outputs}\label{elements-of-data-within-the-inputs-and-outputs}}
\end{itemize}

\hypertarget{when-implementation-decisions-are-made-the-technical-specifications-for-the-interfaces-should-be-added-to-the-dictionary.}{%
\subsubsection{When implementation decisions are made the technical
specifications for the interfaces should be added to the
dictionary.}\label{when-implementation-decisions-are-made-the-technical-specifications-for-the-interfaces-should-be-added-to-the-dictionary.}}

\hypertarget{motivation-27}{%
\subsubsection{Motivation}\label{motivation-27}}

\hypertarget{the-work-context-diagram-provides-an-accurate-definition-of-the-scope-of-the-work-being-studied-and-the-product-scope-diagram-see-sections-8a-8b-defines-the-boundary-of-the-product-to-be-built.-these-definition-can-be-completely-accurate-only-if-the-information-flows-bordering-the-scope-have-their-attributes-defined.}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{The work context diagram provides an
accurate definition of the scope of the work being studied and the
product scope diagram (See Sections 8a \& 8b) defines the boundary of
the product to be built. These definition can be completely accurate
only if the information flows bordering the scope have their attributes
defined.
}{The work context diagram provides an accurate definition of the scope of the work being studied and the product scope diagram (See Sections 8a \& 8b) defines the boundary of the product to be built. These definition can be completely accurate only if the information flows bordering the scope have their attributes defined. }}\label{the-work-context-diagram-provides-an-accurate-definition-of-the-scope-of-the-work-being-studied-and-the-product-scope-diagram-see-sections-8a-8b-defines-the-boundary-of-the-product-to-be-built.-these-definition-can-be-completely-accurate-only-if-the-information-flows-bordering-the-scope-have-their-attributes-defined.}}

\hypertarget{section-17}{%
\subsubsection{}\label{section-17}}

\hypertarget{considerations-16}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Considerations
}{Considerations }}\label{considerations-16}}

\hypertarget{the-dictionary-provides-a-link-between-the-requirementsbusiness-analysts-and-the-designersdevelopersimplementers.-the-implementers-add-implementation-details-to-the-terms-in-the-dictionary-defining-how-the-data-will-be-implemented.-also-implementers-add-terms-that-are-present-because-of-the-chosen-technology-and-that-are-independent-of-the-business-requirements.}{%
\subsubsection{The dictionary provides a link between the
requirements/business analysts and the
designers/developers/implementers. The implementers add implementation
details to the terms in the dictionary, defining how the data will be
implemented. Also, implementers add terms that are present because of
the chosen technology and that are independent of the business
requirements.}\label{the-dictionary-provides-a-link-between-the-requirementsbusiness-analysts-and-the-designersdevelopersimplementers.-the-implementers-add-implementation-details-to-the-terms-in-the-dictionary-defining-how-the-data-will-be-implemented.-also-implementers-add-terms-that-are-present-because-of-the-chosen-technology-and-that-are-independent-of-the-business-requirements.}}

\hypertarget{as-you-study-the-work-you-often-discover-that-an-entry-that-you-have-put-in-the-naming-conventions-and-terminology-section-4-turns-out-to-be-a-specific-flow-of-data-or-an-attribute-data.-when-this-happens-you-should-transfer-the-entry-to-the-data-dictionary.}{%
\subsubsection{As you study the work you often discover that an entry
that you have put in the Naming Conventions and Terminology (section 4)
turns out to be a specific flow of data or an attribute data. When this
happens you should transfer the entry to the data
dictionary.}\label{as-you-study-the-work-you-often-discover-that-an-entry-that-you-have-put-in-the-naming-conventions-and-terminology-section-4-turns-out-to-be-a-specific-flow-of-data-or-an-attribute-data.-when-this-happens-you-should-transfer-the-entry-to-the-data-dictionary.}}

\hypertarget{form-25}{%
\subsubsection{Form}\label{form-25}}

\hypertarget{the-data-dictionary-is-maintained-in-a-variety-of-forms-depending-on-the-tools-that-you-have-at-your-disposal.-the-important-issue-is-that-you-make-it-as-easy-as-possible-to-cross-reference-the-use-of-terms-in-requirements-documents-and-models-with-their-definitions-in-the-dictionary.-common-forms-for-maintaining-the-data-dictionary-are-spreadsheets-databases-and-automated-requirements-tools.}{%
\subsubsection{The data dictionary is maintained in a variety of forms,
depending on the tools that you have at your disposal. The important
issue is that you make it as easy as possible to cross reference the use
of terms in requirements, documents and models with their definitions in
the dictionary. Common forms for maintaining the data dictionary are
spreadsheets, databases and automated requirements
tools.}\label{the-data-dictionary-is-maintained-in-a-variety-of-forms-depending-on-the-tools-that-you-have-at-your-disposal.-the-important-issue-is-that-you-make-it-as-easy-as-possible-to-cross-reference-the-use-of-terms-in-requirements-documents-and-models-with-their-definitions-in-the-dictionary.-common-forms-for-maintaining-the-data-dictionary-are-spreadsheets-databases-and-automated-requirements-tools.}}

\hypertarget{the-scope-of-the-product}{%
\section{8. The Scope of the Product}\label{the-scope-of-the-product}}

\hypertarget{a.-product-boundary}{%
\subsection{8a. Product Boundary}\label{a.-product-boundary}}

\hypertarget{a-use-case-diagram-identifies-the-boundaries-between-the-users-actors-and-the-product.-you-arrive-at-the-product-boundary-by-inspecting-each-business-use-case-and-determining-in-conjunction-with-the-appropriate-stakeholders-which-part-of-the-business-use-case-should-be-automated-or-satisfied-by-some-sort-of-product-and-what-part-should-be-done-by-the-user-or-some-other-product.-this-task-must-take-into-account-the-abilities-of-the-usersactors-section-2-the-constraints-section-3-the-goals-of-the-project-section-1-and-your-knowledge-of-both-the-work-and-the-technology-that-can-make-the-best-contribution-to-the-work.}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{A use case diagram identifies the
boundaries between the users (actors) and the product. You arrive at the
product boundary by inspecting each business use case and determining,
in conjunction with the appropriate stakeholders, which part of the
business use case should be automated (or satisfied by some sort of
product) and what part should be done by the user or some other product.
This task must take into account the abilities of the users/actors
(section 2), the constraints (section 3), the goals of the project
(section 1), and your knowledge of both the work and the technology that
can make the best contribution to the work.
}{A use case diagram identifies the boundaries between the users (actors) and the product. You arrive at the product boundary by inspecting each business use case and determining, in conjunction with the appropriate stakeholders, which part of the business use case should be automated (or satisfied by some sort of product) and what part should be done by the user or some other product. This task must take into account the abilities of the users/actors (section 2), the constraints (section 3), the goals of the project (section 1), and your knowledge of both the work and the technology that can make the best contribution to the work. }}\label{a-use-case-diagram-identifies-the-boundaries-between-the-users-actors-and-the-product.-you-arrive-at-the-product-boundary-by-inspecting-each-business-use-case-and-determining-in-conjunction-with-the-appropriate-stakeholders-which-part-of-the-business-use-case-should-be-automated-or-satisfied-by-some-sort-of-product-and-what-part-should-be-done-by-the-user-or-some-other-product.-this-task-must-take-into-account-the-abilities-of-the-usersactors-section-2-the-constraints-section-3-the-goals-of-the-project-section-1-and-your-knowledge-of-both-the-work-and-the-technology-that-can-make-the-best-contribution-to-the-work.}}

\hypertarget{the-example-use-case-diagram-shows-the-usersactors-outside-the-product-boundary-the-rectangle.-the-product-use-cases-pucs-are-the-ellipses-inside-the-boundary.-the-numbers-link-each-puc-back-to-the-buc-that-it-came-from-see-section-7.-the-arrows-denote-usage.-in-this-version-of-a-puc-diagram-we-put-names-on-the-arrows-to-make-it-more-precise-and-traceable.-note-that-actors-can-be-either-automated-or-human.}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{The example use case diagram shows the
users/actors outside the product boundary (the rectangle). The product
use cases (PUCs) are the ellipses inside the boundary. The numbers link
each PUC back to the BUC that it came from (see section 7). The arrows
denote usage. In this version of a PUC diagram we put names on the
arrows to make it more precise and traceable. Note that actors can be
either automated or human.
}{The example use case diagram shows the users/actors outside the product boundary (the rectangle). The product use cases (PUCs) are the ellipses inside the boundary. The numbers link each PUC back to the BUC that it came from (see section 7). The arrows denote usage. In this version of a PUC diagram we put names on the arrows to make it more precise and traceable. Note that actors can be either automated or human. }}\label{the-example-use-case-diagram-shows-the-usersactors-outside-the-product-boundary-the-rectangle.-the-product-use-cases-pucs-are-the-ellipses-inside-the-boundary.-the-numbers-link-each-puc-back-to-the-buc-that-it-came-from-see-section-7.-the-arrows-denote-usage.-in-this-version-of-a-puc-diagram-we-put-names-on-the-arrows-to-make-it-more-precise-and-traceable.-note-that-actors-can-be-either-automated-or-human.}}

\hypertarget{you-derive-the-pucs-by-deciding-where-the-product-boundary-should-be-for-each-business-use-case-buc.-these-decisions-are-based-on-your-and-appropriate-stakeholders-knowledge-of-the-work-and-the-requirements-constraints.-note-that-the-pucs-that-you-come-up-with-must-be-traceable-back-to-the-bucs.-when-you-implement-a-puc-your-internal-design-might-and-probably-will-mean-that-you-will-implement-a-puc-with-several-system-use-cases-sucs.}{%
\subsubsection{You derive the PUCs by deciding where the product
boundary should be for each business use case (BUC). These decisions are
based on your and appropriate stakeholders' knowledge of the work and
the requirements constraints. Note that the PUCs that you come up with
must be traceable back to the BUCs. When you implement a PUC your
internal design might, and probably will, mean that you will implement a
PUC with several system use cases
(SUCs).}\label{you-derive-the-pucs-by-deciding-where-the-product-boundary-should-be-for-each-business-use-case-buc.-these-decisions-are-based-on-your-and-appropriate-stakeholders-knowledge-of-the-work-and-the-requirements-constraints.-note-that-the-pucs-that-you-come-up-with-must-be-traceable-back-to-the-bucs.-when-you-implement-a-puc-your-internal-design-might-and-probably-will-mean-that-you-will-implement-a-puc-with-several-system-use-cases-sucs.}}

\hypertarget{section-18}{%
\subsubsection{}\label{section-18}}

\hypertarget{example-3}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Example }{Example }}\label{example-3}}

\includegraphics[width=5.96181in,height=3.85486in]{vertopal_7b3017d28f8c463495d83dbfa1d97e53/media/image5.png}

\hypertarget{the-numbers-on-the-puc-diagram-above-correspond-to-the-buc-numbers-on-the-business-event-list-see-section-7.}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{The numbers on the PUC diagram above
correspond to the BUC numbers on the Business Event List (see section
7).
}{The numbers on the PUC diagram above correspond to the BUC numbers on the Business Event List (see section 7). }}\label{the-numbers-on-the-puc-diagram-above-correspond-to-the-buc-numbers-on-the-business-event-list-see-section-7.}}

\hypertarget{you-can-see-that-the-puc-diagram-is-an-effective-summary-for-a-small-number-up-to-around-20-pucs.-if-you-have-a-larger-number-of-pucs-then-a-product-scope-diagram-together-with-a-puc-summary-table-see-8b-is-a-better-approach.}{%
\subsubsection{You can see that the PUC diagram is an effective summary
for a small number (up to around 20) PUCs. If you have a larger number
of PUCs then a Product Scope Diagram together with a PUC Summary Table
(see 8b) is a better
approach.}\label{you-can-see-that-the-puc-diagram-is-an-effective-summary-for-a-small-number-up-to-around-20-pucs.-if-you-have-a-larger-number-of-pucs-then-a-product-scope-diagram-together-with-a-puc-summary-table-see-8b-is-a-better-approach.}}

\hypertarget{below-is-an-example-of-a-product-scope-diagram-for-the-road-de-icing-project.}{%
\subsubsection{Below is an example of a Product Scope Diagram for the
Road De-icing
project.}\label{below-is-an-example-of-a-product-scope-diagram-for-the-road-de-icing-project.}}

\hypertarget{the-content-of-each-one-of-the-interfaces-on-the-product-scope-diagram-is-defined-in-the-data-dictionary-and-can-also-be-supported-by-a-prototype-or-simulation-of-some-kind.-some-projects-publish-a-separate-document-called-the-interface-specification-document.-the-content-of-that-document-would-be-the-definitions-of-the-interfaces-on-the-product-scope-diagram-often-supported-by-prototypes-and-models.}{%
\subsubsection{The content of each one of the interfaces on the product
scope diagram is defined in the data dictionary and can also be
supported by a prototype or simulation of some kind. Some projects
publish a separate document called the Interface Specification Document.
The content of that document would be the definitions of the interfaces
on the Product Scope Diagram often supported by prototypes and
models.}\label{the-content-of-each-one-of-the-interfaces-on-the-product-scope-diagram-is-defined-in-the-data-dictionary-and-can-also-be-supported-by-a-prototype-or-simulation-of-some-kind.-some-projects-publish-a-separate-document-called-the-interface-specification-document.-the-content-of-that-document-would-be-the-definitions-of-the-interfaces-on-the-product-scope-diagram-often-supported-by-prototypes-and-models.}}

\hypertarget{section-19}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{\protect\includegraphics[width=5.9625in,height=3.72292in]{vertopal_7b3017d28f8c463495d83dbfa1d97e53/media/image6.png}}{}}\label{section-19}}

The above Product Scope diagram summarises the interfaces between the
product and the actors/users.

\hypertarget{form-26}{%
\subsubsection{Form}\label{form-26}}

\hypertarget{a-product-use-case-diagram.}{%
\subsubsection{A product use case
diagram.}\label{a-product-use-case-diagram.}}

\hypertarget{a-product-scope-diagram-supported-by-individual-use-case-specification.}{%
\subsubsection{A product scope diagram supported by individual use case
specification.}\label{a-product-scope-diagram-supported-by-individual-use-case-specification.}}

\hypertarget{specifications-and-prototypes-of-the-interfaces-on-the-scope-diagram.}{%
\subsubsection{Specifications and prototypes of the interfaces on the
scope
diagram.}\label{specifications-and-prototypes-of-the-interfaces-on-the-scope-diagram.}}

\hypertarget{b.-product-use-case-table}{%
\subsection{8b. Product Use Case
Table}\label{b.-product-use-case-table}}

\hypertarget{the-product-scope-diagram-is-a-useful-summary-of-all-the-interfaces-between-the-product-and-other-automated-systems-organizations-and-users.-if-there-are-a-manageable-number-of-pucs-say-less-than-twenty-then-the-puc-diagram-is-useful-as-a-graphical-way-of-summarizing-the-pucs-relevant-to-the-product-but-in-practice-we-have-found-that-a-product-use-case-table-is-more-useful-because-it-can-handle-larger-numbers-of-pucs-and-it-precisely-identifies-the-input-and-output-data-that-defines-the-boundary-of-each-puc.}{%
\subsubsection{The product scope diagram is a useful summary of all the
interfaces between the product and other automated systems,
organizations and users. If there are a manageable number of PUC's --
say less than twenty -- then the PUC diagram is useful as a graphical
way of summarizing the PUC's relevant to the product, But in practice we
have found that a Product Use Case Table is more useful because it can
handle larger numbers of PUCs and it precisely identifies the input and
output data that defines the boundary of each
PUC.}\label{the-product-scope-diagram-is-a-useful-summary-of-all-the-interfaces-between-the-product-and-other-automated-systems-organizations-and-users.-if-there-are-a-manageable-number-of-pucs-say-less-than-twenty-then-the-puc-diagram-is-useful-as-a-graphical-way-of-summarizing-the-pucs-relevant-to-the-product-but-in-practice-we-have-found-that-a-product-use-case-table-is-more-useful-because-it-can-handle-larger-numbers-of-pucs-and-it-precisely-identifies-the-input-and-output-data-that-defines-the-boundary-of-each-puc.}}

\hypertarget{this-is-where-you-define-the-details-about-the-individual-product-use-cases-pucs-listed-on-your-puc-table.-you-can-include-a-scenario-or-model-for-each-product-use-case-on-your-list.}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{This is where you define the details
about the individual product use cases PUCs listed on your PUC table.
You can include a scenario or model, for each product use case on your
list.
}{This is where you define the details about the individual product use cases PUCs listed on your PUC table. You can include a scenario or model, for each product use case on your list. }}\label{this-is-where-you-define-the-details-about-the-individual-product-use-cases-pucs-listed-on-your-puc-table.-you-can-include-a-scenario-or-model-for-each-product-use-case-on-your-list.}}

\hypertarget{form-27}{%
\subsubsection{Form}\label{form-27}}

• A text scenario

• A storyboard

• A low fi prototype

• A hi fi prototype

• A formal use case specification including exceptions and alternatives

• A sequence diagram, activity diagram, dataflow diagram, or any other
type of model that is familiar to your project group

\hypertarget{functional-requirements-1}{%
\section{\texorpdfstring{9. Functional Requirements
}{9. Functional Requirements }}\label{functional-requirements-1}}

Requirements}\label{a.-functional-requirements}}

\hypertarget{content-29}{%
\subsubsection{Content}\label{content-29}}

\hypertarget{this-is-a-specification-for-each-atomic-functional-requirement.-as-for-all-types-of-atomic-requirementsfunctional-non-functional-constraint-use-the-requirements-shell-as-a-guide-for-which-attributes-should-be-specified.-a-full-explanation-of-the-atomic-requirement-and-its-attributes-is-included-in-this-templates-introductory-material.}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{This is a specification for each atomic
functional requirement. As for all types of atomic
requirements(functional, non-functional, constraint), use the
requirements shell as a guide for which attributes should be
specified\emph{.} A full explanation of the atomic requirement and its
attributes is included in this template's introductory
material.}{This is a specification for each atomic functional requirement. As for all types of atomic requirements(functional, non-functional, constraint), use the requirements shell as a guide for which attributes should be specified. A full explanation of the atomic requirement and its attributes is included in this template's introductory material.}}\label{this-is-a-specification-for-each-atomic-functional-requirement.-as-for-all-types-of-atomic-requirementsfunctional-non-functional-constraint-use-the-requirements-shell-as-a-guide-for-which-attributes-should-be-specified.-a-full-explanation-of-the-atomic-requirement-and-its-attributes-is-included-in-this-templates-introductory-material.}}

product.}\label{to-specify-the-detailed-functional-requirements-to-be-carried-out-by-the-product.}}

\hypertarget{examples-14}{%
\subsubsection{Examples}\label{examples-14}}

\hypertarget{section-35}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{\protect\includegraphics[width=5.95833in,height=3.70347in]{vertopal_7b3017d28f8c463495d83dbfa1d97e53/media/image7.pct}}{}}\label{section-35}}

\hypertarget{section-36}{%
\subsubsection{}\label{section-36}}

\hypertarget{fit-criterion}{%
\subsubsection{Fit Criterion}\label{fit-criterion}}

\hypertarget{each-functional-requirement-should-have-a-fit-criterion-or-a-test-case.-in-any-event-the-fit-criterion-is-the-benchmark-so-that-the-tester-can-objectively-determine-whether-or-not-the-implemented-product-has-met-the-requirement.}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Each functional requirement should have a
fit criterion or a test case. In any event, the fit criterion is the
benchmark so that the tester can objectively determine whether or not
the implemented product has met the requirement.
}{Each functional requirement should have a fit criterion or a test case. In any event, the fit criterion is the benchmark so that the tester can objectively determine whether or not the implemented product has met the requirement. }}\label{each-functional-requirement-should-have-a-fit-criterion-or-a-test-case.-in-any-event-the-fit-criterion-is-the-benchmark-so-that-the-tester-can-objectively-determine-whether-or-not-the-implemented-product-has-met-the-requirement.}}

\hypertarget{considerations-17}{%
\subsubsection{Considerations}\label{considerations-17}}

\hypertarget{if-you-have-produced-an-eventuse-case-list-see-sections-6c-and-8ab-then-you-can-use-it-to-help-you-trigger-the-functional-requirements-for-each-eventuse-case.-if-you-have-not-produced-an-eventuse-case-list-give-each-functional-requirement-a-unique-number-and-to-help-with-traceability-partition-these-requirements-into-eventuse-caserelated-groups-later-in-the-development-process.}{%
\subsubsection{If you have produced an event/use case list (see sections
6c and 8a/b), then you can use it to help you trigger the functional
requirements for each event/use case. If you have not produced an
event/use case list, give each functional requirement a unique number
and, to help with traceability, partition these requirements into
event/use case--related groups later in the development
process.}\label{if-you-have-produced-an-eventuse-case-list-see-sections-6c-and-8ab-then-you-can-use-it-to-help-you-trigger-the-functional-requirements-for-each-eventuse-case.-if-you-have-not-produced-an-eventuse-case-list-give-each-functional-requirement-a-unique-number-and-to-help-with-traceability-partition-these-requirements-into-eventuse-caserelated-groups-later-in-the-development-process.}}

\hypertarget{note-that-if-you-have-not-identified-the-product-boundary-and-are-not-in-a-position-to-determine-the-product-use-cases-pucs-then-write-the-functional-and-non-functional-requirements-for-the-business-use-cases-bucs.-this-is-an-especially-good-strategy-if-you-are-writing-business-requirements-and-asking-suppliers-to-tell-you-which-of-your-business-requirements-can-be-satisfied-by-their-products.}{%
\subsubsection{Note that if you have not identified the product boundary
and are not in a position to determine the product use cases (PUC's),
then write the functional and non-functional requirements for the
business use cases (BUC's). This is an especially good strategy if you
are writing business requirements and asking suppliers to tell you which
of your business requirements can be satisfied by their
product/s.}\label{note-that-if-you-have-not-identified-the-product-boundary-and-are-not-in-a-position-to-determine-the-product-use-cases-pucs-then-write-the-functional-and-non-functional-requirements-for-the-business-use-cases-bucs.-this-is-an-especially-good-strategy-if-you-are-writing-business-requirements-and-asking-suppliers-to-tell-you-which-of-your-business-requirements-can-be-satisfied-by-their-products.}}

\hypertarget{form-28}{%
\subsubsection{Form}\label{form-28}}

\hypertarget{the-form-that-you-use-to-capture-and-maintain-your-atomic-requirements-functional-non-functional-and-constraint-depends-on-the-tools-that-you-have-available-to-you.-volere-snow-cards-are-often-a-useful-aid-to-help-you-in-discovering-requirements-but-due-to-volume-and-need-to-be-able-to-make-changes-some-kind-of-automated-form-is-the-best-way-to-manage-and-maintain-your-atomic-requirements.-common-forms-for-atomic-requirements-are}{%
\subsubsection{The form that you use to capture and maintain your atomic
requirements (functional, non-functional and constraint) depends on the
tools that you have available to you. Volere snow cards are often a
useful aid to help you in discovering requirements but, due to volume
and need to be able to make changes, some kind of automated form is the
best way to manage and maintain your atomic requirements. Common forms
for atomic requirements
are:}\label{the-form-that-you-use-to-capture-and-maintain-your-atomic-requirements-functional-non-functional-and-constraint-depends-on-the-tools-that-you-have-available-to-you.-volere-snow-cards-are-often-a-useful-aid-to-help-you-in-discovering-requirements-but-due-to-volume-and-need-to-be-able-to-make-changes-some-kind-of-automated-form-is-the-best-way-to-manage-and-maintain-your-atomic-requirements.-common-forms-for-atomic-requirements-are}}

• A spreadsheet (a sample is included with the download of this
template)

• A database provided with whatever requirements tool/s you have
available. There is a wide variety of tools on the market, refer to
http://www.volere.co.uk/tools for a list

• An intranet set up by you to maintain and make accessible the atomic
requirements and their attributes

• A custom built database

Whatever form you use to record and maintain your requirements, it is
important to be consistent with your numbering and terminology so that
you can check for completeness and respond to change.

\hypertarget{non-functional-requirements-1}{%
\section{Non-functional
Requirements}\label{non-functional-requirements-1}}

\emph{The following sections 10-17 describe the non-functional
requirements. The form of these requirements is the same as for the
functional requirements as described above.}

relating to the spirit of the product. Your client may have made
particular demands for the product, such as corporate branding, colours
to be used, and so on. This section captures the requirements for the
appearance. Do not attempt to design it until the appearance
requirements are known.
}{The section contains requirements relating to the spirit of the product. Your client may have made particular demands for the product, such as corporate branding, colours to be used, and so on. This section captures the requirements for the appearance. \hypertarget{b.-style-requirements}{%
\subsection{\texorpdfstring{10b. Style Requirements
}{10b. Style Requirements }}\label{b.-style-requirements}}

\hypertarget{content-31}{%
\subsubsection{Content}\label{content-31}}

consistency with other packages put out by your organization. Keep in
mind the European laws on packaging, which require that the package not
be significantly larger than the product it encloses.

Keep in mind the European laws on packaging, which require that the package not be significantly larger than the product it encloses. }}\label{in-this-section-you-would-also-describe-the-appearance-of-the-package-if-this-is-to-be-a-manufactured-product.-the-package-may-have-some-requirements-as-to-its-size-style-and-consistency-with-other-packages-put-out-by-your-organization.-keep-in-mind-the-european-laws-on-packaging-which-require-that-the-package-not-be-significantly-larger-than-the-product-it-encloses.}}

the designers to create a product as envisioned by your
client.}\label{the-style-requirements-that-you-record-here-will-guide-the-designers-to-create-a-product-as-envisioned-by-your-client.}}

\hypertarget{motivation-30}{%
\subsubsection{Motivation}\label{motivation-30}}

\hypertarget{given-the-state-of-todays-market-and-peoples-expectations-we-cannot-afford-to-build-products-that-have-the-wrong-style.-once-the-functional-requirements-are-satisfied-it-is-often-the-appearance-and-style-of-products-that-determine-whether-they-are-successful.-your-task-in-this-section-is-to-determine-precisely-how-the-product-shall-appear-to-its-intended-consumer.}{%
\subsubsection{Given the state of today's market and people's
expectations, we cannot afford to build products that have the wrong
style. Once the functional requirements are satisfied, it is often the
appearance and style of products that determine whether they are
successful. Your task in this section is to determine precisely how the
product shall appear to its intended
consumer.}\label{given-the-state-of-todays-market-and-peoples-expectations-we-cannot-afford-to-build-products-that-have-the-wrong-style.-once-the-functional-requirements-are-satisfied-it-is-often-the-appearance-and-style-of-products-that-determine-whether-they-are-successful.-your-task-in-this-section-is-to-determine-precisely-how-the-product-shall-appear-to-its-intended-consumer.}}

\subsubsection{Considerations}\label{considerations-19}}

\hypertarget{the-look-and-feel-requirements-specify-your-clients-vision-of-the-products-appearance.-the-requirements-may-at-first-seem-to-be-rather-vague-e.g.-conservative-and-professional-appearance-but-these-will-be-quantified-by-their-fit-criteria.-the-fit-criteria-give-you-the-opportunity-to-extract-from-your-client-precisely-what-is-meant-and-give-the-designer-precise-instructions-on-what-he-is-to-accomplish.}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{The look and feel requirements specify
your client's vision of the product's appearance. The requirements may
at first seem to be rather vague (e.g., ``conservative and professional
appearance''), but these will be quantified by their fit criteria. The
fit criteria give you the opportunity to extract from your client
precisely what is meant, and give the designer precise instructions on
what he is to accomplish.
}{The look and feel requirements specify your client's vision of the product's appearance. The requirements may at first seem to be rather vague (e.g., ``conservative and professional appearance''), but these will be quantified by their fit criteria. The fit criteria give you the opportunity to extract from your client precisely what is meant, and give the designer precise instructions on what he is to accomplish. }}\label{the-look-and-feel-requirements-specify-your-clients-vision-of-the-products-appearance.-the-requirements-may-at-first-seem-to-be-rather-vague-e.g.-conservative-and-professional-appearance-but-these-will-be-quantified-by-their-fit-criteria.-the-fit-criteria-give-you-the-opportunity-to-extract-from-your-client-precisely-what-is-meant-and-give-the-designer-precise-instructions-on-what-he-is-to-accomplish.}}

\hypertarget{usability-and-humanity-requirements}{%
\section{11. Usability and Humanity
Requirements}\label{usability-and-humanity-requirements}}

This section is concerned with requirements that make the product usable
and ergonomically acceptable to its hands-on users.

\hypertarget{a.-ease-of-use-requirements}{%
\subsection{\texorpdfstring{11a. Ease of Use Requirements
}{11a. Ease of Use Requirements }}\label{a.-ease-of-use-requirements}}

\hypertarget{content-32}{%
\subsubsection{Content}\label{content-32}}

\hypertarget{this-section-describes-your-clients-aspirations-for-how-easy-it-is-for-the-intended-users-of-the-product-to-operate-it.-the-products-usability-is-derived-from-the-abilities-of-the-expected-users-of-the-product-and-the-complexity-of-its-functionality.}{%
\subsubsection{This section describes your client's aspirations for how
easy it is for the intended users of the product to operate it. The
product's usability is derived from the abilities of the expected users
of the product and the complexity of its
functionality.}\label{this-section-describes-your-clients-aspirations-for-how-easy-it-is-for-the-intended-users-of-the-product-to-operate-it.-the-products-usability-is-derived-from-the-abilities-of-the-expected-users-of-the-product-and-the-complexity-of-its-functionality.}}

as

\subsubsection{● Efficiency of use: How quickly or accurately the user
can use the
product.}\label{efficiency-of-use-how-quickly-or-accurately-the-user-can-use-the-product.}}

product.}\label{ease-of-remembering-how-much-the-casual-user-is-expected-to-remember-about-using-the-product.}}

\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{● Error rates: For some products it is
crucial that the user commits very few, or no, errors.
}{● Error rates: For some products it is crucial that the user commits very few, or no, errors. }}\label{error-rates-for-some-products-it-is-crucial-that-the-user-commits-very-few-or-no-errors.}}

\hypertarget{overall-satisfaction-in-using-the-product-this-is-especially-important-for-commercial-interactive-products-that-face-a-lot-of-competition.-web-sites-are-a-good-example.}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{● Overall satisfaction in using the
product: This is especially important for commercial, interactive
products that face a lot of competition. Web sites are a good example.
}{● Overall satisfaction in using the product: This is especially important for commercial, interactive products that face a lot of competition. Web sites are a good example. }}\label{overall-satisfaction-in-using-the-product-this-is-especially-important-for-commercial-interactive-products-that-face-a-lot-of-competition.-web-sites-are-a-good-example.}}

\subsubsection{● Feedback: How much feedback the user needs to feel
confident that the product is actually accurately doing what the user
expects. The necessary degree of feedback will be higher for some
products (e.g., safety-critical products) than for
others.}\label{feedback-how-much-feedback-the-user-needs-to-feel-confident-that-the-product-is-actually-accurately-doing-what-the-user-expects.-the-necessary-degree-of-feedback-will-be-higher-for-some-products-e.g.-safety-critical-products-than-for-others.}}

configurability of the product. Configurability allows different users
to have different functional variations of the product.
}{You might also consider the configurability of the product. Configurability allows different users to have different functional variations of the product. }}\label{you-might-also-consider-the-configurability-of-the-product.-configurability-allows-different-users-to-have-different-functional-variations-of-the-product.}}

\hypertarget{c.-learning-requirements}{%
\subsection{\texorpdfstring{11c. Learning Requirements
}{11c. Learning Requirements }}\label{c.-learning-requirements}}

\hypertarget{content-34}{%
\subsubsection{Content}\label{content-34}}

\hypertarget{requirements-specifying-how-easy-it-should-be-to-learn-to-use-the-product.-this-learning-curve-ranges-from-zero-time-for-products-intended-for-placement-in-the-public-domain-e.g.-a-parking-meter-or-a-web-site-to-a-considerable-amount-of-time-for-complex-highly-technical-products.-we-know-of-one-product-where-it-was-necessary-for-graduate-engineers-to-spend-18-months-in-a-training-program-before-being-qualified-to-use-the-product.}{%
\subsubsection{Requirements specifying how easy it should be to learn to
use the product. This learning curve ranges from zero time for products
intended for placement in the public domain (e.g., a parking meter or a
web site) to a considerable amount of time for complex, highly technical
products. (We know of one product where it was necessary for graduate
engineers to spend 18 months in a training program before being
qualified to use the
product.)}\label{requirements-specifying-how-easy-it-should-be-to-learn-to-use-the-product.-this-learning-curve-ranges-from-zero-time-for-products-intended-for-placement-in-the-public-domain-e.g.-a-parking-meter-or-a-web-site-to-a-considerable-amount-of-time-for-complex-highly-technical-products.-we-know-of-one-product-where-it-was-necessary-for-graduate-engineers-to-spend-18-months-in-a-training-program-before-being-qualified-to-use-the-product.}}

\hypertarget{motivation-33}{%
\subsubsection{Motivation}\label{motivation-33}}

\hypertarget{to-quantify-the-amount-of-time-that-your-client-feels-is-allowable-before-a-user-can-successfully-use-the-product.-this-requirement-guides-designers-to-understand-how-users-will-learn-the-product.-for-example-designers-may-build-elaborate-interactive-help-facilities-into-the-product-or-the-product-may-be-packaged-with-a-tutorial.-alternatively-the-product-may-have-to-be-constructed-so-that-all-of-its-functionality-is-apparent-upon-first-encountering-it.}{%
\subsubsection{To quantify the amount of time that your client feels is
allowable before a user can successfully use the product. This
requirement guides designers to understand how users will learn the
product. For example, designers may build elaborate interactive help
facilities into the product, or the product may be packaged with a
tutorial. Alternatively, the product may have to be constructed so that
all of its functionality is apparent upon first encountering
it.}\label{to-quantify-the-amount-of-time-that-your-client-feels-is-allowable-before-a-user-can-successfully-use-the-product.-this-requirement-guides-designers-to-understand-how-users-will-learn-the-product.-for-example-designers-may-build-elaborate-interactive-help-facilities-into-the-product-or-the-product-may-be-packaged-with-a-tutorial.-alternatively-the-product-may-have-to-be-constructed-so-that-all-of-its-functionality-is-apparent-upon-first-encountering-it.}}

\hypertarget{examples-18}{%
\subsubsection{Examples}\label{examples-18}}

\hypertarget{the-product-shall-be-easy-for-an-engineer-to-learn.}{%
\subsubsection{The product shall be easy for an engineer to
learn.}\label{the-product-shall-be-easy-for-an-engineer-to-learn.}}

\hypertarget{a-clerk-shall-be-able-to-be-productive-within-a-short-time.}{%
\subsubsection{A clerk shall be able to be productive within a short
time.}\label{a-clerk-shall-be-able-to-be-productive-within-a-short-time.}}

\hypertarget{the-product-shall-be-able-to-be-used-by-members-of-the-public-who-will-receive-no-training-before-using-it.}{%

\hypertarget{d.-understandability-and-politeness-requirements}{%
\subsection{11d. Understandability and Politeness
Requirements}\label{d.-understandability-and-politeness-requirements}}

\begin{quote}
This section is concerned with discovering requirements related to
concepts and metaphors that are familiar to the intended end users.
\end{quote}

\hypertarget{content-35}{%
\subsubsection{Content}\label{content-35}}

\hypertarget{this-specifies-the-requirement-for-the-product-to-be-understood-by-its-users.-while-usability-refers-to-ease-of-use-efficiency-and-similar-characteristics-understandability-determines-whether-the-users-instinctively-know-what-the-product-will-do-for-them-and-how-it-fits-into-their-view-of-the-world.-you-can-think-of-understandability-as-the-product-being-polite-to-its-users-and-not-expecting-them-to-know-or-learn-things-that-have-nothing-to-do-with-their-business-problem.-another-aspect-of-politeness-is-that-the-product-should-not-expect-the-user-to-input-any-information-to-which-the-product-already-has-access.}{%
\subsubsection{This specifies the requirement for the product to be
understood by its users. While ``usability'' refers to ease of use,
efficiency, and similar characteristics, ``understandability''
determines whether the users instinctively know what the product will do
for them and how it fits into their view of the world. You can think of
understandability as the product being polite to its users and not
expecting them to know or learn things that have nothing to do with
their business problem. Another aspect of politeness is that the product
should not expect the user to input any information to which the product
already has
access.}\label{this-specifies-the-requirement-for-the-product-to-be-understood-by-its-users.-while-usability-refers-to-ease-of-use-efficiency-and-similar-characteristics-understandability-determines-whether-the-users-instinctively-know-what-the-product-will-do-for-them-and-how-it-fits-into-their-view-of-the-world.-you-can-think-of-understandability-as-the-product-being-polite-to-its-users-and-not-expecting-them-to-know-or-learn-things-that-have-nothing-to-do-with-their-business-problem.-another-aspect-of-politeness-is-that-the-product-should-not-expect-the-user-to-input-any-information-to-which-the-product-already-has-access.}}

\hypertarget{motivation-34}{%
\subsubsection{Motivation}\label{motivation-34}}

\hypertarget{to-avoid-forcing-users-to-learn-terms-and-concepts-that-are-part-of-the-products-internal-construction-and-are-not-relevant-to-the-users-world.-to-make-the-product-more-comprehensible-and-thus-more-likely-to-be-adopted-by-its-intended-users.}{%
\subsubsection{To avoid forcing users to learn terms and concepts that
are part of the product's internal construction and are not relevant to
the users' world. To make the product more comprehensible and thus more
likely to be adopted by its intended
users.}\label{to-avoid-forcing-users-to-learn-terms-and-concepts-that-are-part-of-the-products-internal-construction-and-are-not-relevant-to-the-users-world.-to-make-the-product-more-comprehensible-and-thus-more-likely-to-be-adopted-by-its-intended-users.}}

\hypertarget{examples-19}{%
\subsubsection{Examples}\label{examples-19}}

\subsubsection{The product shall use symbols and words that are
naturally understandable by the user
community.}\label{the-product-shall-use-symbols-and-words-that-are-naturally-understandable-by-the-user-community.}}

\hypertarget{the-product-shall-hide-the-details-of-its-construction-from-the-user.}{%

}{Refer to section 2d, Hands-On Users of the Product, and consider the world from the point of view of each of the different types of users. }}\label{refer-to-section-2d-hands-on-users-of-the-product-and-consider-the-world-from-the-point-of-view-of-each-of-the-different-types-of-users.}}

\hypertarget{in-many-countries-it-is-required-that-some-products-be-made-available-to-the-disabled.-in-any-event-it-is-self-defeating-to-exclude-this-sizable-community-of-potential-customers.}{%

\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Some users have disabilities other than

A simple, and not very consequential, example is that approximately 20 percent of males are red-green colour-blind. }}\label{some-users-have-disabilities-other-than-the-commonly-described-ones.-in-addition-some-partial-disabilities-are-fairly-common.-a-simple-and-not-very-consequential-example-is-that-approximately-20-percent-of-males-are-red-green-colour-blind.}}

\hypertarget{performance-requirements}{%
\section{12. Performance Requirements}\label{performance-requirements}}

\hypertarget{a.-speed-and-latency-requirements}{%
\subsection{12a. Speed and Latency
Requirements}\label{a.-speed-and-latency-requirements}}

\hypertarget{content-37}{%
\subsubsection{Content}\label{content-37}}

\hypertarget{specifies-the-amount-of-time-available-to-complete-specified-tasks.-these-requirements-often-refer-to-response-times.-they-can-also-refer-to-the-products-ability-to-operate-at-a-speed-suitable-for-the-intended-environment.}{%
\subsubsection{Specifies the amount of time available to complete
specified tasks. These requirements often refer to response times. They
can also refer to the product's ability to operate at a speed suitable
for the intended
environment.}\label{specifies-the-amount-of-time-available-to-complete-specified-tasks.-these-requirements-often-refer-to-response-times.-they-can-also-refer-to-the-products-ability-to-operate-at-a-speed-suitable-for-the-intended-environment.}}

\hypertarget{motivation-36}{%
\subsubsection{Motivation}\label{motivation-36}}

\hypertarget{some-productsusually-real-time-productsmust-be-able-to-perform-some-of-their-functionality-within-a-given-time-slot.-failure-to-do-so-may-mean-catastrophic-failure-e.g.-a-ground-sensing-radar-in-an-airplane-fails-to-detect-an-upcoming-mountain-or-the-product-will-not-cope-with-the-required-volume-of-use-e.g.-an-automated-ticket-selling-machine.}{%
\subsubsection{Some products---usually real-time products---must be able
to perform some of their functionality within a given time slot. Failure
to do so may mean catastrophic failure (e.g., a ground-sensing radar in
an airplane fails to detect an upcoming mountain) or the product will
not cope with the required volume of use (e.g., an automated
ticket-selling
machine).}\label{some-productsusually-real-time-productsmust-be-able-to-perform-some-of-their-functionality-within-a-given-time-slot.-failure-to-do-so-may-mean-catastrophic-failure-e.g.-a-ground-sensing-radar-in-an-airplane-fails-to-detect-an-upcoming-mountain-or-the-product-will-not-cope-with-the-required-volume-of-use-e.g.-an-automated-ticket-selling-machine.}}

\hypertarget{examples-21}{%

\subsubsection{Fit Criterion}\label{fit-criterion-5}}

\hypertarget{fit-criteria-are-needed-when-the-description-of-the-requirement-is-not-quantified.-however-we-find-that-most-performance-requirements-are-stated-in-quantified-terms.-the-exception-is-the-second-requirement-shown-above-for-which-the-suggested-fit-criterion-is}{%

is}\label{fit-criteria-are-needed-when-the-description-of-the-requirement-is-not-quantified.-however-we-find-that-most-performance-requirements-are-stated-in-quantified-terms.-the-exception-is-the-second-requirement-shown-above-for-which-the-suggested-fit-criterion-is}}

\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{The product shall respond in less than 1
second for 90 percent of the interrogations. No response shall take
longer than 2.5 seconds.
}{The product shall respond in less than 1 second for 90 percent of the interrogations. No response shall take longer than 2.5 seconds. }}\label{the-product-shall-respond-in-less-than-1-second-for-90-percent-of-the-interrogations.-no-response-shall-take-longer-than-2.5-seconds.}}

\hypertarget{considerations-25}{%
\subsubsection{Considerations}\label{considerations-25}}

\hypertarget{there-is-a-wide-variation-in-the-importance-of-different-types-of-speed-requirements.-if-you-are-working-on-a-missile-guidance-system-then-speed-is-extremely-important.-by-contrast-an-inventory-control-report-that-is-run-once-every-six-months-has-very-little-need-for-a-lightning-fast-response-time.}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{There is a wide variation in the
importance of different types of speed requirements. If you are working
on a missile guidance system, then speed is extremely important. By
contrast, an inventory control report that is run once every six months
has very little need for a lightning-fast response time.
}{There is a wide variation in the importance of different types of speed requirements. If you are working on a missile guidance system, then speed is extremely important. By contrast, an inventory control report that is run once every six months has very little need for a lightning-fast response time. }}\label{there-is-a-wide-variation-in-the-importance-of-different-types-of-speed-requirements.-if-you-are-working-on-a-missile-guidance-system-then-speed-is-extremely-important.-by-contrast-an-inventory-control-report-that-is-run-once-every-six-months-has-very-little-need-for-a-lightning-fast-response-time.}}

\hypertarget{customize-this-section-of-the-template-to-give-examples-of-the-speed-requirements-that-are-important-within-your-environment.}{%

of the speed requirements that are important within your
environment.}\label{customize-this-section-of-the-template-to-give-examples-of-the-speed-requirements-that-are-important-within-your-environment.}}

must

\hypertarget{considerations-26}{%
\subsubsection{Considerations}\label{considerations-26}}

\hypertarget{the-example-requirements-given-here-apply-to-some-but-not-all-products.-it-is-not-possible-to-give-examples-of-every-variation-of-safety-critical-requirement.-to-make-the-template-work-in-your-environment-you-should-customize-it-by-adding-examples-that-are-specific-to-your-products.}{%
\subsubsection{The example requirements given here apply to some, but
not all, products. It is not possible to give examples of every
variation of safety-critical requirement. To make the template work in
your environment, you should customize it by adding examples that are
specific to your
products.}\label{the-example-requirements-given-here-apply-to-some-but-not-all-products.-it-is-not-possible-to-give-examples-of-every-variation-of-safety-critical-requirement.-to-make-the-template-work-in-your-environment-you-should-customize-it-by-adding-examples-that-are-specific-to-your-products.}}

\hypertarget{also-be-aware-that-different-countries-have-different-safety-standards-and-laws-relating-to-safety.-if-you-plan-to-sell-your-product-internationally-you-must-be-aware-of-these-laws.-a-colleague-has-suggested-that-for-electrical-products-if-you-follow-the-german-standards-the-largest-number-of-countries-will-be-supported.}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Also, be aware that different countries
have different safety standards and laws relating to safety. If you plan
to sell your product internationally, you must be aware of these laws. A
colleague has suggested that for electrical products, if you follow the
German standards, the largest number of countries will be supported.
}{Also, be aware that different countries have different safety standards and laws relating to safety. If you plan to sell your product internationally, you must be aware of these laws. A colleague has suggested that for electrical products, if you follow the German standards, the largest number of countries will be supported. }}\label{also-be-aware-that-different-countries-have-different-safety-standards-and-laws-relating-to-safety.-if-you-plan-to-sell-your-product-internationally-you-must-be-aware-of-these-laws.-a-colleague-has-suggested-that-for-electrical-products-if-you-follow-the-german-standards-the-largest-number-of-countries-will-be-supported.}}

\hypertarget{if-you-are-building-safety-critical-systems-then-the-relevant-safety-critical-standards-are-already-well-specified.-you-will-likely-have-safety-experts-on-your-staff.-these-experts-are-the-best-source-of-the-relevant-safety-critical-requirements-for-your-type-of-product.-they-will-almost-certainly-have-copious-information-that-you-can-use.}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{ If you are building safety-critical
systems, then the relevant safety-critical standards are already well
specified. You will likely have safety experts on your staff. These
experts are the best source of the relevant safety-critical requirements
for your type of product. They will almost certainly have copious
information that you can
use.}{ If you are building safety-critical systems, then the relevant safety-critical standards are already well specified. You will likely have safety experts on your staff. These experts are the best source of the relevant safety-critical requirements for your type of product. They will almost certainly have copious information that you can use.}}\label{if-you-are-building-safety-critical-systems-then-the-relevant-safety-critical-standards-are-already-well-specified.-you-will-likely-have-safety-experts-on-your-staff.-these-experts-are-the-best-source-of-the-relevant-safety-critical-requirements-for-your-type-of-product.-they-will-almost-certainly-have-copious-information-that-you-can-use.}}

\hypertarget{consult-your-legal-department.-members-of-this-department-will-be-aware-of-the-kinds-of-lawsuits-that-have-resulted-from-product-safety-failure.-this-is-probably-the-best-starting-place-for-generating-relevant-safety-requirements.}{%
\subsubsection{Consult your legal department. Members of this department
will be aware of the kinds of lawsuits that have resulted from product
safety failure. This is probably the best starting place for generating
relevant safety
requirements.}\label{consult-your-legal-department.-members-of-this-department-will-be-aware-of-the-kinds-of-lawsuits-that-have-resulted-from-product-safety-failure.-this-is-probably-the-best-starting-place-for-generating-relevant-safety-requirements.}}

\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Avoid stating how you would design a
solution to the security requirements. For instance, don't specify a
password system. Your aim here is to identify the security requirement;
the design will come from the requirement.
}{Avoid stating how you would design a solution to the security requirements. For instance, don't specify a password system. Your aim here is to identify the security requirement; the design will come from the requirement. }}\label{avoid-stating-how-you-would-design-a-solution-to-the-security-requirements.-for-instance-dont-specify-a-password-system.-your-aim-here-is-to-identify-the-security-requirement-the-design-will-come-from-the-requirement.}}

\hypertarget{consider-asking-for-help.-computer-security-is-a-highly-specialized-field-and-one-where-improperly-qualified-people-have-no-business.-if-your-product-has-need-of-more-than-average-security-we-advise-you-to-make-use-of-a-security-consultant.-such-consultants-are-not-cheap-but-the-results-of-inadequate-security-can-be-even-more-expensive.}{%
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Consider asking for help. Computer
security is a highly specialized field, and one where improperly
qualified people have no business. If your product has need of more than
average security, we advise you to make use of a security consultant.
Such consultants are not cheap, but the results of inadequate security
can be even more expensive.
}{Consider asking for help. Computer security is a highly specialized field, and one where improperly qualified people have no business. If your product has need of more than average security, we advise you to make use of a security consultant. Such consultants are not cheap, but the results of inadequate security can be even more expensive. }}\label{consider-asking-for-help.-computer-security-is-a-highly-specialized-field-and-one-where-improperly-qualified-people-have-no-business.-if-your-product-has-need-of-more-than-average-security-we-advise-you-to-make-use-of-a-security-consultant.-such-consultants-are-not-cheap-but-the-results-of-inadequate-security-can-be-even-more-expensive.}}

after a fire destroys their computer systems. Integrity requirements are
aimed at preventing complete loss, as well as corruption, of data and
processes.

For example, almost half of small businesses go bankrupt after a fire destroys their computer systems. Integrity requirements are aimed at preventing complete loss, as well as corruption, of data and processes. }}\label{organizations-are-relying-more-and-more-on-their-stored-data.-if-this-data-should-be-come-corrupt-or-incorrector-disappearthen-it-could-be-a-fatal-blow-to-the-organization.-for-example-almost-half-of-small-businesses-go-bankrupt-after-a-fire-destroys-their-computer-systems.-integrity-requirements-are-aimed-at-preventing-complete-loss-as-well-as-corruption-of-data-and-processes.}}

\subsubsection{Question whether the product is intended for a culture
other than the one with which you are familiar. Ask whether people in
other countries or in other types of organizations will use the product.
Do these people have different habits, holidays, superstitions, or
cultural norms that do not apply to your own culture? Are there colours,
icons, measurement units or words that have different meanings in
another cultural environment? If your reaction to a requirement is --
that's rather odd/unusual/weird then likely you have a cultural
requirement.}\label{question-whether-the-product-is-intended-for-a-culture-other-than-the-one-with-which-you-are-familiar.-ask-whether-people-in-other-countries-or-in-other-types-of-organizations-will-use-the-product.-do-these-people-have-different-habits-holidays-superstitions-or-cultural-norms-that-do-not-apply-to-your-own-culture-are-there-colours-icons-measurement-units-or-words-that-have-different-meanings-in-another-cultural-environment-if-your-reaction-to-a-requirement-is-thats-rather-oddunusualweird-then-likely-you-have-a-cultural-requirement.}}

\hypertarget{project-issues-1}{%
\section{Project Issues}\label{project-issues-1}}

The following \emph{sections 18-27} contain issues that must be faced if
the requirements are to be met and the product to become a reality.
These sections also connect the requirements with the project activities
that discover and progress the requirements. If you are using a
consistent language for communicating requirements then project managers
can use the requirements as input to steering the project. The Volere
Requirements Knowledge Model (included with the download of Version 16
of the template) provides the basis for a requirements common language
by identifying classes of requirements knowledge and the relationships
between them. Each of the classes of knowledge is cross-referenced to
sections in this template.

\hypertarget{off-the-shelf-solutions}{%
\section{19. Off-the-Shelf Solutions}\label{off-the-shelf-solutions}}

This section looks at available solutions and summarizes their
applicability to the requirements. This discussion is not intended to be
a full feasibility study of the alternatives, but it should tell your
client that you have considered some alternatives and determined how
closely they match the requirements for the product.

buy a solution, the amount of effort to modify and install a ready-made
solution, and so on.

\hypertarget{migration-to-the-new-product}{%
\section{22. Migration to the New
Product}\label{migration-to-the-new-product}}

When you install a new product, some things always have to be done
before it can work successfully. For example, databases often have to be
converted. There is usually new data to be collected, procedures to be
converted, and many other steps to be taken to ensure the successful
transition to the new product.

Often there are periods where the organization will run both the old
product and the new product in parallel until the new one has proven
that it is functioning correctly.

This section of the specification is where you identify the tasks
necessary for the period of transition to the new product. This section
is input to the project planning process.

\hypertarget{a.-requirements-for-migration-to-the-new-product}{%

Product}\label{a.-requirements-for-migration-to-the-new-product}}
